Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which, one way is that you make three or four cauteries, lining them along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery of the liver that we have described before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and the patient should often lie on their back; and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart that is near the mouse, or if the patient's pain comes from the left, and the elevation by which you lift the heart should be along the heart, along the length of the body, and the cauteries should be along the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, insert the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, you can cauterize with a cautery of three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment, when it has cast off corruption for a long time, and this is worth more than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for a person with dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does not work, then you should make four cauteries around the abdomen, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one on the breast; and let the cauteries be close to the thick part of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to discharge corruption for a long time, and do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be joined together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the clavicle that we have shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is mentioned before.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is hydrops, and are full of yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and annular; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, lest the yellow water be forced out, and let the cauteries be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the shinbone; and let the cauteries be long, one under the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without treating, so that the water comes out; afterwards, treat with the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When a stomach ailment comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by other methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with strong constitution, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what was discussed earlier, regarding the cautery of the stomach, a circular cautery; and four cauteries around the small of the back with small, pointed cauteries, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering greatly, then make a cautery on the groin, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach next to the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of gross, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have described in the divisions, but are not improving, then make cauteries: three along the spine of the back, gradually moving from the edges to the middle, in a triangular pattern, and one cautery below the small of the back at the buttocks.  And if you think the patient's stomach is cold and the food is not digesting, and you see the face swelling, then make one large cautery on the stomach as previously mentioned, and one other on the liver and another on the spleen using a pointed cautery. Leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment, keep the area clean until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul," heat the cautery, which resembles a razor, and then place it fully ignited onto the cut "thelul";  keep your hand there until the cautery reaches the beginning of the vein, where the blood flows; do this once or twice. If there is a lot of "thelul," cauterize each part as we have described; afterwards, treat with beneficial ointments until healed. And if you cauterize a large cautery on the tumor, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	Of a poorly healed wound.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or incision, as we will describe in its place, such an illness comes that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes upon someone, and is old and throws off corruption and putrid moisture, you should probe it with a very fine probe, and be careful to ascertain how deep the fistula is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Afterwards, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the depth that the probe has entered, and repeat the cauterization until the putrid and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to its need; and beware of burning the nerves and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder or the intestines, be wary of these areas and only perform the cauterization in fleshy areas, and be sure it is not penetrating; afterwards, heal the area until it is healthy, and if the area is sealed, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is perforated, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted; and thus, as one of those that we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the illness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great windiness, and does not take the form of a woman's complaint, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the kidneys on one side and the other, with the clavil cautery that we have previously mentioned; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and it will give greater aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and cold from moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then cauterize the outside of the bladder, where the hair of the lancet begins, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the width of one finger; and you make one cautery on the back outside, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be clavil shaped, according to the form previously described.
de la marris	Of the gall bladder
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the gall bladder is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their endings delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the pouch, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the outside of the back; and let the cauteries be clavil-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the hip joint, and because of this it moves from its place, and the sign is that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of separation is found to be empty, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip joint with one circular cautery, and mark the area around the joint, following its contour, so that the joint is inside the circle; and let the cautery be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated as we have said in the division and the treatment is not working, and the illness is old, then you must purge the patient of the thick humors with foul-smelling pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, apply cautery; and the method of cautery is of two types: that is to say, medicines that burn, and cautery by fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cautery by fire is in many ways, one of which is this: you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make them good and deep, and have a space of one finger's breadth between each cautery, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes cautery is made in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we previously mentioned regarding the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire hip, and all the thick parts of the hip are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, then make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, a little to the left side; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and let the thick part of the hip be burned; and if the patient feels the pain extend to the toes of the foot or near the toes, cauterize it there where he feels the pain three or four times with the cautery called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, more cauteries are made; and if you know the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have made cauteries on the ankle of the foot, and left them on so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot also, and the entire foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly, from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cauteries in one and the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones said, concerning the cautery of the hip, that the method is this: make an iron like this, and let it be at the head as thick as a fingernail, or a little less, and let it be with grooves and from one groove to the other the space of a thumb's breadth; and let the grooves be opposite each other and be like knots, and let there be a handle of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then one places it on the affected hip area, and let it be turned towards the healthy side; and cauterize one time, one cautery round, and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open a long time; after the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we rarely use this cautery because of the fear of its effect, and we see few who use it; and nevertheless, this is a good cautery, for whoever can endure it, and in the place where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you make an instrument with grooves in which the edge of the gate descends, and let it be of bronze or iron with one long side, and in height let it have two widths, and let there be between each the thickness of a finger; and let them be open in front and above, and let them join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Afterwards, place it on the patient's hip area, lying on their healthy side, and press your hand firmly on the hip area; then pour between the two circles of warm water that has been heated slightly in the fire, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is a burning effect there, just like from fire; and when the burning effect has passed, remove your hand with the instrument and wash the hip area with soft water, and leave it like this for three days, and apply butter until what is black from the scalding is removed; and leave it for three days so that any rot will come out; and that would be the final help after treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds water in the same way as you did for the hip; and this is the manner of the warm water, and I have written it in the treatment of the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole to let a razor point enter; and put another pot, well sealed, on top of that pot, and put alkali and lime and soft water on top, until there is a finger's breadth of it on top of the powders when you have grasped it well with your hand; and leave it like that until it descends water and drips into the sealed pot, then take all that water, and pour it over lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in ways of medical practices and cauterizations of other limbs. For it does as much work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip in the same way as turpentine and honey and anacardi and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen recounts a cure by which a man was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatic vein, and praises it highly, and says that no other cure was made, and that he was healed in one single instance when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as he will teach here next.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And says in this way that you take fresh and dry green litharge, and grind it finely with a little fat, and place it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bandage it; and let it remain for three hours, and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter the bath until his body is slightly wet, and put him in bed, and the pain will disappear and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps greatly; and the cauteries should be made in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow between the big toe and the other, which is called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards, take dry goat dung, and heat it in fire until it is embers, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished; and repeat this, and do not stop doing this until you think by feeling that it reaches the hip, and that the pain is stopped; and this method of cautery is called "cautery of the goat".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from percussion or from excessive evacuation, or from a spreading cold matter, no cautery is worthwhile for any of these, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has been rid of fetid pills or similar things, to make three lines of incisions on the back, where the pain is located, and in each line five cauteries, or more, according to the strength and the amount that the patient can endure; and the cauteries should be made in the manner of the cautery called "points"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries in the middle clavile cautery, according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow gait when they rise, and fear; and you find in the final spine of the back and in the appearance of the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery encompasses each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a piercing cautery of two or three lines, and the points should be close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After curing the area until it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery to swelling that is in the space of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is from moisture spread throughout the body's limbs, and when the pain is in the feet, which the physicians properly call "podagra," and when it is caused by cold and medicine cannot cure it, it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick above the sole of the foot, then make a cautery in the form of what is called a "point" cautery.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains extend to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, then make three or four cauteries on each knee, of the olive-shaped cautery type; and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold your hand there any longer than is necessary for the depth of the heart to be burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks around the wrist, two lines apart; and if any pain remains in the fingers, make pricks on each joint and above the skin of the hand; and if the pains extend to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge phlegm, he will be healthy with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the surface
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture occurs in the groin, and the bowels descend to the testicles, and it is recent, then when you wish to cure it, he must not eat that day; and let him use things that loosen the belly, so that the feces descend from his belly; afterward, make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath until the bowels are repaired, and return them to your fingers, and make a mark under the rupture on the bone of the thigh, and make a mark of the shape of half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and throws off sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then return the bowels to their place, and let the attendant hold his hand over them so they do not return; and open the patient's thighs well, and place a cushion and a servant on the thighs, and another on the chest who holds his hands; then place the cautery over the mark with your whole hand, hold it straight, and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you reach the bone; and beware carefully that the bowels do not jump out when you apply the cautery; that you do not burn them; and that by this the patient does not die, or another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and for large people as large according to their size; after three days, treat the cautery site with butter until the heat is gone; after that, treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on their back for 40 days until the wound is properly sealed; and it is necessary that their nourishment be light for a long time, so that the bowels do not jump out when he attempts to walk around.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wishes to get up, let the attendant provide him with a good bandage, and keep it on for another 40 days; and let him have good rest, let him not work much, and avoid excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and when he follows this instruction he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now discuss the treatment of cutting in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other parts of the belly and are recognized, and you see that they are not growing, apply a cautery of the appropriate size to the area, and let a third of the center of the wound be burned; afterwards, treat it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a cautery in three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the location of the incision and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another outside it, and place your hand in the middle to apply the entire cautery to the wound.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cures of medicine do not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a cautery called "poins," and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness, weakness, and virtue, and its location of twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, repeat another cautery on top of that one, for such is the custom that it must move to the limb that is closest to it, for which it is necessary that you do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of phlegm
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Phlegm is sometimes helped greatly by cautery, especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it to be cauterized, be careful if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and does not descend or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may seize the entire patient, then give it five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, another toward the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and leave your hand there until the cauteries reach the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the mice as it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the phlegm is spread throughout; and it visibly departs, you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the rump and another beside it, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, that you do not burn them; and sometimes one does cauteries on the bone of the fist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more you help, and the more benefit you give; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And the cauteries should be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the place with flour of wheat with honey and other cures until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then you shall make cauteries on the limb according to the size and smallness of the limb; and let the cauteries be a little deep into the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cauteries are made on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and nevertheless, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sickness called "albaras" is aged, and the tools of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the amount of flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of wheat and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and some blood of a colon and blood of an almond, each a part; and mix them all together, and bind it with a cloth, and let it air in the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre begins, and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet, the wise say that one should also cauterize the middle of the chancre; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it might become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen on a few occasions; and a more correct thing is that it be cauterized around it, with the cautery called "circular", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it is slow to heal, either because of the superfluity it causes, or because of the age of the sick person when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of the time; and you want to hasten its healing: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it with the entire cautery, then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the core, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them from the outside in such a way that the course of the decay is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After that, treat it until it is healed perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment by fire iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of disease called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a gnawing of the limbs, for it devours the members just as fire devours dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the disease is; afterwards cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it three days, and put on the cauterized areas a soft poultice with oil until the heat from the fire is gone, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment with ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on whatever part of the corrupted areas remains.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ailment is sometimes cured with sharp medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already discussed the cure with sharp medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the sores that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often there comes a disease on the feet, called "closure" according to our understanding, and is a large, enclosed thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this illness are in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is this: heat a cautery, shaped like a vaulted roof, made of good iron, sized to encompass the nail on all sides and with fine edges; after it's very hot, put it on the nail head and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; leave it there for three days until it begins to cast off pus; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows and salt, and leave it on all night; the nail will fall out and be rooted out.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with a healing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by outward causes, and often occur on hands and feet, you must apply hot water cautery.  Do this: take a copper or iron rod, or a vaulted roof-shaped tool, and place it on the nail and the wart;  put the rod around it completely, then put a little hot water on it and hold it firmly; press your hand around so the rod's edge reaches the nail's root, and the hot water can find a deep passage to the root; let the patient endure the hot water's slight burning for an hour; leave it like this, and the nail will be completely rooted out.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this repeatedly, until you have removed all those that are on the body, then treat them with healing ointments.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold nerves, or from a fever of quartan or other, you should apply four cauteries along the spine, one between each vertebra; and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with a cautery-shaped tool; this will stop the trembling and hasten recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Pustules that stink.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes, foul-smelling pustules appear on the body, caused by corrupted, thick matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	When they first appear, you should apply a cautery to each head of the pustule: a thin cautery of myrtle wood, whose tip has been heated in fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lens-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the start when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluities from which they arise are broken up and they heal; but this should be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often, there are large bleedings from the artery cut in the open wound, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and in similar cases; and it is a very serious matter to stanch the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to anyone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it firmly until the blood is stilled beneath your finger and no more drops issue; then heat several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then grasp one, either large or small, according to the wound and the location where the artery is ruptured, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cautery has gone out, quickly take another cautery from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this, one after the other, until the blood is stanched; and be careful not to burn the nerve nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood spurts from the artery, it cannot be well stanched, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is not treated, or by strong binding of thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stanch blood; and let it be bandaged and pressed accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies the stanching by tightly binding with cloths or putting burning things on, or other similar things, will achieve little to no benefit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they have neither a bandage nor medicine available, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and firmly press until it is stanched on the wound and on the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water frequently, so that it is very cold, until the blood is frozen and thickened and stanched; and do as necessary with whatever cauteries and medicines are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on the cures of wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	In the first chapter, we have told you about every ailment requiring cautery with fire or burning medicine, and the origins, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have arranged that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter in the same way so that one may find more easily whatever one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, dear son, you must understand that this chapter contains more danger and fear than the first on cauteries, and therefore requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	for there come some who become so enraged with their illness that they die easily because of the frenzy they find in their illness, and from the greatness of its malice; and one should fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who give you their senses, and say, "wait, I am cured"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more emphasis on your honor than your greed, and do not work foolishly, but wisely, with those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can have taken and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your patients, to which health may be converted; and this will help you acquire good renown, and glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and may He inspire you with His holy inspiration, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter in divisions, according to what is before, or the chapter on cauteries, which I have explained from head to toe, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children during childbirth, when the midwife squeezes the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from a cause that is unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness outside of children, and death came quickly to all those I have seen; and therefore it seems to me that I had better leave such treatments alone.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew larger each day until it could not support it; and the swelling grew so much that he died, and this swelling has gathered under the bone on the surface, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such if the swelling is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make a wide fissure in the middle of the head; and be as long as two fingers, until the swelling runs; and see here the form of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the swelling is more extensive, and the abscess is larger, make two fissures in the form of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the swelling is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the sutures of the head open on each side, and the water spurts out when you press your hand against it inside, and this is not responded to: then you must make three fissures in the middle of the head in this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the swelling.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, bind the fissures with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then remove the dressings, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and leave the head to heal evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strong and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look at where the swelling of the abscess and the gathering of water are; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut where the abscess and the collection of water are apparent, and cut it according to your ability; and be careful not to cut the artery; and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the discharge of blood and the evacuation of swelling.
de reume	of phlegm
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in their eyes or chest, and the illness is longstanding, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last cure is cautery, with which the two arteries will be cut.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you intend to cut them, the patient must tilt their head back; after that, rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient must tighten their neck completely with the cloth; then, look for where the veins branch, and the locations of both arteries are behind the ears, and are close together; then mark the locations accurately, then cut one and the other with a sharp scalpel from two sides, until the cut reaches the bone, and this is to be along the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you want, place the scalpel beneath the artery and cut above it, cutting as you would to pierce through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will spurt out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the arteries do not appear when touched, you must measure the space of three fingers, then mark it precisely and cut down to the bone; and the amount of blood to be released is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on the patient's ability to endure and the fullness of the artery; then examine the wound: if any portion of pus remains on the bone, cut it so that no more festering occurs, then bandage the wound and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of a migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and old-fashioned madness and similar things, and he is treated with various medical cures and none of it does him any good, then we will open the arteries in the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should pull back the hair on their temples and locate the artery that appears in the temple, for it appears clearly by its throbbing, and is rarely visible except in some very cold individuals; and if it is visible, the patient must restrain its neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and soak the area with hot water until the artery is clearly apparent; then take the spatula, of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then gently scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues beneath on each side; and if the artery is thin, turn it with the point of the needle, then cut it off with that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not completely stop flowing.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain blood from six ounces to three; and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that no decay occurs before the wound is closed, and blood does not ooze out; then cut away the excess tissue between the two ligatures at the same time, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a surgical cautery to the bone until the tissue is cut; and that is the best work if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are a help for finishing off moisture; for this reason, they are of even greater assistance for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the area with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; and when one removes them, it should be treated with dry medicines that promote tissue growth and bandages until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery while you are working on it, quickly stop it by cauterizing it, or fill the area with vitriol and hold it with your hand to stop the blood; and if you don't have that available, place your finger on the area until the blood is congealed, and rinse the area with cold water until the bleeding stops and is constricted as necessary; and the best and easiest way to extract an artery is to cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery from two sides, but the sharp parts should be well spaced to maintain their heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one finger's width of space between the two blades, and then when you have marked the two places, you place the hot iron on top until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and the two edges should be separated, for it is not entirely fused by this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears from the eyes are running down the veins on the top of the head, and no medical treatment helps, and you see the patient's forehead turning red and feeling tremors like shivers; and the skin is thin and moist so that the hairs of the temples are falling out and the temples are burned and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "contusive treatment," and what you do for the patient with this illness is to remove the hair from their forehead, then make three equal cuts on the forehead along its length; and one cut should be about two fingers wide, going straight down from the middle of the forehead towards the nose, and the other two are on either side of the temples, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on either side of the temples; and keep your hand away from the line of the two jaws, and each incision should be about three fingers wide through and through; and have a piece of sponge and many cloths ready to wipe the blood away, then apply the pointed spatula from both sides, which is the shape:
