des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision next to the temple to the second incision; and burn all the flesh between the two incisions to the whole surface above the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then place the instrument called a "cultellaire" into the first incision; it is very sharp on one side, and gentle on the other, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh next to the flesh, and the gentle edge towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what appears of the flesh, and then do the same in the middle incision until the other incision; and then drain the blood as well, and press the area for the extracted blood; then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put wet cloths in wine, oil, and vinegar over them, and ensure no hot abscesses form there; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and apply a lot of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment and rose oil, and other treatments for healing wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When some come with acute catarrh, and you see the eyes dull and small, and the sight weakening, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and the head aches sharply, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that these matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the best remedy for it is this one.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you order the patient to lie on their back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one from the width of a fingernail.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood away with a sponge, and then separate the two sides of the incision and place old cotton and linen bandages; then tie wet cloths in wine and oil on top, and watch out for a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with things that dry up and make flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to make flesh grow all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a stone or similar thing like iron; or seeds, like peas, beans, or lentils; or a flowing thing, like water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other object falls into the ear that does not adhere to or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then drip a little violet oil or oil of sesame, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with a condiment, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and extend the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often, pus comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then administer extraction with subtle forceps, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with the forceps, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a thin, small-doubled hook; and if it does not come out with that, then make a small copper wire loop and insert the loop into the ear canal firmly, and seal that which is around the loop with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the loop; then pull strongly, for often pus comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, then take some birdlime and put on it some tool that is suitable for doing this, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever, and pull for pus to come out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with any of these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear before a hot abscess or spasm occurs; and the method of the incision is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to its strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, near the fat or dependent area; and let the incision be like a crescent, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and quickly suck it into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin, subtle spatule according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do that when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with thin forceps and by sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing remedies, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it stops flowing because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many stones according to the length of your finger, light and small, and warm them a little in the fire; and let the patient put one or more into their ear, and jump on them with their feet on the other side, and push another stone onto the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop placing stone on stone until all the water comes out, and thus it all comes out; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and hold the other end over fire until the softest part of the reed is burned; then repeat this with other reeds until the water comes out entirely, as we have said of the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of a creature, if it is small, like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms lodged in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment is of no use, then you must examine the ear in the sunlight: if any worms are visible, extract them with fine tweezers, and if not visible, take the tool with which their form is displayed:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow at the bottom and wide at the top.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the finest end into the ear according to the severity of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly on the entire tool; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then stuff around the tool with cotton as I said for the stone; and if they do not jump out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the removal of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and you should distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this tool, whose shape you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or bronze, narrow at the bottom with a small hole, and wide at the top for distilling; and to push the distillation inside, use a well-made bronze tool for this, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you want, into the tool, and the tool should be in the ear; then place the scraper with all the cotton inside, and press with your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillations be a little heated by the fire before distilling it into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No children are born without holes in their ears; and this same thing happens to adults through the blockage of a wound, or from flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is a slight opening of the hole, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which goes deep, so that one cannot see it, requires a more serious treatment in several ways, and for that which one can see, you must place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage clearly, then use this instrument for cleaning, whose shape is shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and cutting at the front and back, completely smooth, so that it does not injure the ear; if the blockage is from flesh that has grown or a growth in the ear, then use very fine tweezers, and carefully cut it out, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the blockage is deep within the ear, then take a fine, light scraper and heat it slightly over a fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel a blockage that the patient feels painful when they hear, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the ear nerves; then place a tent inside the ear, matching the size of the opening, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is closed, or you take a tent and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another tent moistened in a cerate made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a discharge of blood occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and apply it to the ear, and use other treatments that stop the blood discharge, which are found in the section on treating discharges.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papules
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This affliction, which comes as papules on the eyes when they are moist and dry, you should carefully pull them with tweezers and pliers, and cut them from their roots with a spatula; then apply powdered vitriol to the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and after the incision, cauterize again; and many times they return, if any part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, papules appear on the eyes that resemble hail in shape and hardness; therefore, this disease is called "hail," and is a collection of thick moisture in the papule above and below; the procedure is this: watch if the hail moves from one side to the other, and that is an easy thing to know; then cut it out widely, and gently scrape it from each part, then remove it with tweezers and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the papule a little, do not harm the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not exert any force, because the ointment will restore it quickly and produce flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the inner ear towards the upper part, turn the papule inside out, and remove the hail with tweezers, and cut and press it on each side; and if the papule is separated by the incision, no harm is done; and when the hail is cut out, wash the area with salty water, and treat the area with something that will produce flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is generated in webs on the eye's papules, and this occurs more often in children than in adults, and it causes great pain in their eyes, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at the sun's light because their tears rush to their eyes; and therefore they lie on their faces often, and sleep on their faces, and their skin under their eyebrows is dampened as the swelling and appearance are covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of treatment is for the patient to place their head on your lap; then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach in each part, then place it over it; and press with your fingers on either side, so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle; then cut through the middle of the moisture with a sharp instrument, making a slit not wider than the incision made when opening a vein; and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exinach; and in several places, exinach comes out of the slit, in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then pull it out completely with a piece of cloth gripped between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to get deeper into the slit, so you don't reach the whole instrument down to the eye, and do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the slit, slightly enlarge the slit a little until it appears; then remove it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place over the area, and bind tightly with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some who grind salt and apply it to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess arises in the area, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When extra hairs grow on the eyelids, besides the natural ones, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause various ailments such as constant tears and softening of the eyelids and albuginea, so that this is a cause for destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery using fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your own, then turn the eyelid to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, put a needle with a thread on it; and let it be next to the eyelid's edge where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and pull the thread over the whole eyelid, and turn it with a razor; then cut in the part under the eyelid, under the extra hairs, throughout the entire area, cutting from the large tear duct down to the small one; then pull out the thread, and put a small cotton and cloth tent under the eyelid, then draw on the eyelid a figure of a bandage, like the leaf of a myrtle, and all the time, the figure must be according to the size you wish to elevate the eyelid which is divided into parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one needs to cut a large amount of the eyelid, according to how the eyelid is softened; then cut throughout the entire area on the two lines you have marked, and begin from the large tear duct up to the small one; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs, the thickness of a root; then insert the lancet into one of the two angles of the tear sac, then scrape it all off; then bring the two edges together with a suture of a needle with a fine wool thread, and dry the blood, and dry the excess threads on the two eyebrows with some sticky substance, if you want to do so; and if not, don't worry about it, then leave the suture and the threads until three or four days; then treat the wound without suture with dry and constricting substances, for the eyelid rises again at the moment of healing of the wound and its joining together, but the suture is harder (as the ancients said), and this is a safe procedure; and there is another method: and that is that you mark the eyelid with a figure that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three separated incisions according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you lack the strength to hold the tweezers, and the things are not equal, take a needle with thread, and insert it into the middle of the figure; and insert another thread next to the large tear duct, and the second thread next to the small one, and join the threads between your fingers equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described, then bring the two edges of the wound together by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms at your incision, calm it with ointments and similar soothing remedies; and sometimes the eyelid's hair is turned inward: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one or the other is more sophisticated.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the eyelids is according to this method: and that is that you turn the eyelid inward and cut it according to what I have said, and then make two stitches, and two fine threads, as long as the eyelid and the width of the area are; and cut at the two ends on both sides where you hold the threads; then join one to the other subtly on what is above the eyelid, and tightly hold the two edges on both sides; and leave it like this for some days, and the skin that is pinched will die and wither and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and the eyelid is raised, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the shape of the two stitches you will make according to this figure, and according to this amount of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put a soft and fine silk thread on it; then join the ends and tie them subtly, and let the thread be one palm long; then place another fine silk thread in the groove briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head on your lap; and let it be near the sun so that the work is clear, for it is a delicate and meticulous work, then insert the needle along the entire groove into the root of the added hair, and pierce the eyelid quickly until you pull it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it is over the groove, and put the hair, if there is one or two or three or more, in the groove; then move your hand until the hairs come out of the entire groove in the eyelid with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the groove is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, pull the groove underneath the entire thread that you have placed in it, until the groove comes out through the hole above and you see it through the eye's vision; then pull out the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and the skin grows; and if the hair is small, attach a long hair from the natural eyebrows, and leave it with it until it lengthens and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati," or rot, comes to the eye, there are two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through wounding, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is to split the wound, separate the edges, and place linen strips inside, and bind it until healed; and you should not use anything drying and constricting in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and irrigate with water or boiled linseed and melted diachylon in some oil, wrap a bandage with it, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the key to your treatment is to ensure it does not heal according to its previous form; and these procedures we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental part comes from wounds, cuts, cauterization, and similar things; and the method of treatment is to take a needle with a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, piercing it from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at two points in the flesh; then stretch the skin over the entire needle, and cut it with a broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the membrane returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a scraper and place it in the fissure, turn the membrane, and make two cuts on the inside of the membrane; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you have made, and form an angle so that when they are joined, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "I griesche"; then remove the flesh, according to how sharp its edges are beneath, from what surrounds the membrane, then join the two separated parts and stitch them with a woolen thread; then treat it with the softeners and dressings we have mentioned, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut, suture, or cauterization, you must make a full incision under the hairs of the membranes, as described above; then separate between the two edges of a dressing, as I have said; and one should perform the treatment according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and skilled masters devise instruments with all their power how to restore the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is required in terms of treatment and instruments in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	Immediately after the membrane.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion occurs in such a way that the membrane above is adhered to the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a scraper under the membrane and lift it; and extend it with forceps, until you cut what is obstructing it with a fine spatula, which must not be too sharp or too sharp, so that the patient cannot tolerate the spatula being too sharp and injuring the eye; and your incision, with which you scrape that adhesion, should be gentle, so that the membrane returns to its natural shape; and the entire adhesion is healed, and sometimes they apply salty water to the eye, and wash it with fresh water and broth; then place a linen dressing between the membrane and the eye, and place wool soaked in abundant egg white on the eye; and after the third day, use broth and healing substances until healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two types: one is nervous and resembles a hard surface, and another that is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and you try to remove with forceps, you cannot; and both types begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; you lift the membrane with your hand, then hold the nail with small forceps, and extend it upwards; then take a needle and insert a horse's, cow's, or ox's hair, and a strong thread; and slightly curve the point of the needle and insert it into the nail, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it upwards, and scrape the side of the nail that touches the pupil and the fibers with the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining portion at the root of the tear duct with a fine spatula and small forces, and leave the natural tissue of the tear duct so that the flow of tears is not disturbed by the incision; and sometimes the nail is extended with a hook alone, and with thread, as we have said; then scrape it with a soft spatula, the shape of which is like this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch and break the fleshy tissue, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision, place a little bruised flax and lead-based broth into the eye, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the hook cannot enter, this type of nail growth is often treated with medicines; and it grows, as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye, and take a slightly pointed, thin spatula according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully scrape the nail upward, and if you see that it diminishes and the base approaches, then distill lead-based broth and red lead-based broth from your mouth into the eye, and bandage the eye until the next day; then resume the other operation according to this same method, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing else wrong in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then drain it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the operation as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the tear duct tissue harms the eye greatly, then hold it with the hook, and cut off a portion, and not all, so that the flow of tears is not obstructed; then distill red lead-based broth into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows, covering the pupil and extending over the eyelids, appearing like a rose-colored blister.  The procedure is for the patient to place their head in your lap, then open their eyes.  You grasp all of that flesh with suitable hooks, and hold it firmly.  Then, cut away the initial flesh, continuing to shave off more until it is removed.  Be careful not to injure the eye during the procedure. The incision should be like the spatumile technique we described for nail removal, with light pressure used to remove debris.  As demonstrated later in this chapter, follow this method. When the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, fill the eye with a mixture of pounded rock salt or distill red lead-based broth and other corrosive medicines; put a bandage made of linen over the eye, to help ensure it doesn't become a hot abscess. If anything remains and a hot abscess threatens, leave the eye and treat the abscess using remedies for hot abscesses.  Return to your procedure once the abscess is healed. This same process is used for any flesh growth in the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must apply treatment to each eye that is weak by natural means and by accidental means, using iron. Do not place your hand into any of these procedures until you see that the limbs can withstand the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins are those that are visible over the eye, impairing its function and weakening the eye daily.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first, examine if the eye, where the debris is, is strong, and if no other illness exists besides the debris. Then grasp it this way: instruct the patient to place their head in your lap, then grasp those veins with a hook according to your wisdom. The hooks must be double and thin according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two hooks, step by step, on one body according to this form.
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then with the hooks, gently grasp those veins, and wipe the blood drop by drop, until you see the removal of those veins from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the hooks, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only cut the veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red gall to corrupt what remains of the debris.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove everything at that time, then apply a plaster to the eye, made of things that soothe the eye's pain, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and any signs of a hot abscess are gone. Then start again in the same manner as before until the eye is healed. And this is the form of treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and with a sharp burning medicine, as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a way to open it above the abscess, where it should remain, and remove all the moisture, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, clean it thoroughly with the instrument described; and it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron, with a sharp point, and be sharpened like a file, as shown in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the decayed part of the bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little, until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the area is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the swelling is healed, and it remains like this for forty days, and it does not re-open or become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other way than to return the fistula to its original opening, according to this method:  you must expose the bone a second time, by means of iron and sharp medicines; and when it is exposed, take a drill according to this form, and let the iron point have three angles, and the shaft be tapered to a point as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, and turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it by the air escaping if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the area with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the area hardens, the matter goes into the nose; this is a less troublesome thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the flow from the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are completely open, and there is no trouble in the nose, nor any lessening, you must bind the patient; then, treat him, then apply cupping glasses or leeches, without hurting them, for suction; then place over the eye a bandage made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocoll; then compress the eye, and put the poultice over it with bandages and strips; and the method for the strips is that you take strips soft enough, and double each into four, and then put one over the other according to the quantity the eye needs; then compress it firmly with a hard bandage, and start the cupping again for suction without harming; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the bandage softens, you must compress it tightly; then remove the bandage after day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice, strips, bandage, and cupping until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the tearing of the web (or cloth) of the eye.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear occurs in the eye's web, it then opens, and fluid comes out of the membranes like grains of resin, and is frightening to see; then if you want to close it, the work is to insert a needle at the base of the affected area down to the top, then insert another needle where there is a doubled thread from the tear duct area; and pierce it, and leave the first needle in its position; then cut the double thread, and tie a portion of the eye around it and compress it well; then remove the needle and place soaked wool moistened with egg white over the eye; and leave it until the thread detaches from the eye, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held together by the eye with a bandaged circle until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows significant signs, then pierce it with a thin, fine spear that goes deep into the eye, and drain the albuminous moisture and bring the eye down, and quickly enter it; then compress it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the swelling of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This ailment, called "alcunnati," is nothing more than a swelling that gathers in the eye, resembling a descending fluid, but it is not fluid; and the procedure for its appearance is to have the patient sit on a prepared, straight-backed chair, then hold the head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the swelling rise before your eyes; then it should enter, not descend, and the light should be clear, and the patient should see things as they used to; and if it does not descend, know that it is an infection, and if the descent of the swelling is not as described, then…
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then, place the patient between your hands, take a fine lancet, and pierce the corneal membrane slightly along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, instill warm, medicated water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled and mixed with honey, into the eye, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of eye infections.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already described the symptoms of infections in the division, and what is necessary for piercing;  therefore, practice accordingly to the healing.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and hold the healthy eye tightly; then place the eye cover in your left hand if the affected eye is on the left, or in your right hand if the affected eye is on the right; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand, if the affected eye is left, or in your left hand, if the affected eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown, about the width of a finger, in the white part of the eye, near the tear duct, then firmly insert the "almagda" instrument, and move your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and the measurement of the almagda's path should be from the depth of the area from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the crown of the eye; you will see the bone in that area because of the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument where the infection is, and press it in turns.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the infection subsides now, the patient can see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, if the infection rises again, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and no longer rises, gently remove the almagda by slowly turning your hand; and then add a small amount of gemstone salt to the infection, and rinse the eye with this.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply a bandage of wool or linen soaked in rose oil and egg white to the affected eye, and secure it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, place a bandage soaked in egg white over it.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men whose eyes are too hard, you must take the instrument called "alberit," of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then place the almagda in it, as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare a comfortable bed for the patient, where he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and keep him free from all movement, and let him eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and let him be bound according to his condition for three days; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then reapply the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary to do this during or immediately after the incision, but it is necessary to delay it, because the infection rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If a hot abscess comes, unbind the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with what soothes abscesses; and when it has calmed down, unbind the eye and place a covering over it for a few days, and let him remain in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then gradually leave the room, and return to his normal activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they make almagdas by piercing, from which they draw out the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similar forms of almagdas, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they are properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And their heads shall be of this same fineness, and the back in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various extra flesh grows on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs; and sometimes there is flesh deeply embedded, of a dark color, and sometimes soft flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that soft flesh, not embedded, you must have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, and apply the lancet to that flesh, and draw it out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp, thin spatula on one side, until you know all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, you must remove it with all the fine instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if it is inflamed or a deep abscess, treat it as is appropriate; and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then apply to the nose easily and sharply, wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens, and moisture comes down to the palate, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is flesh growing on the bone above, which the instruments do not reach to cut; then you must place a fairly thick linen thread, tied in your hands, and a space of a finger or less between each knot; and the patient should push the thread end into their nose as far as possible, and pull it while smelling until it comes from the nose into the mouth; and children often do this at school, and it is an easy task for whoever wants to do it; then hold the end coming from the nose in one hand, and the other end coming from the mouth in the other hand, and pull them alternately while holding the knots that are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have dissolved that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all remaining flesh; and then place a lead strip in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the method for purifying the nose, by which oils and medicines are instilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, like a strip, and the conduit as well; and if you wish, make a closed strip, and let the instrument be full to purify the nose; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease called "telul" arises in the area of the nose, and it grows and becomes large, so that it's a frightening sight; and for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it entirely, then place a cautery or burning medicine on the site; and if one delays cutting it until it's large, be aware if it is hard, of a dark color, and without sensation: do not touch it with iron, for it is a festering abscess, because when it is cut sometimes, it will lead to great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be entirely cut out, then drain the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the area with drying and astringent things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come upon one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, check if the wound is fresh and completely free of blood; then bring the two edges together with stitches, and treat it until it is healed.  And if the edges are already separated on either side, you must scorch all parts of their edges until they bleed, then bring the two edges together with stitches and tighten it, and sprinkle on powder of dragon's blood and crushed incense; and place a piece of strong plaster or another binding plaster over the powders, and leave it until it comes off on its own, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you bring the solution together: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	Of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.
