In some people, hard abscesses develop within the lips, resembling grains of millet, sometimes small, sometimes large; then it is necessary that you turn back the lips, and make incisions on each bump, and grasp it with forceps and cut it in each part; then fill the space after the incision with crushed vitriol, until the bleeding has stopped; and then remove any pus, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, extra flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should grasp it with pliers, and cut it at its root, and allow the pus or blood to drain; then apply crushed vitriol or other astringent and drying powders to the area; and if the flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: it will not return after cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of sores.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, hard, rough scales form at the base of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, and decayed, so that the decay spreads to the gums, and the teeth stink; you should have the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your grasp, and scrape away the scales or any visible discoloration, until nothing remains; do the same for black spots, green spots, yellowing, and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if you remove all the affected parts on the first try, that's good; otherwise, repeat the process on the second and third days, until everything is cleaned; and know that teeth require various tools for scraping, depending on what the craftsman demonstrates, because the scrapers used for cleaning the surfaces of the teeth have different shapes than those used for scraping between the teeth; and these various tools should be prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a toothache, you should delay extracting it as long as possible, for this should not be done; for it is a very difficult procedure until there is no other option for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is forced to have the tooth extracted, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often, the pain will mislead the patient, and they believe it's in a healthy tooth, and a healthy tooth is extracted; and nevertheless, the pain does not disappear because of this bad extraction, as we have already seen this happen with our esteemed patients; and when you are sure of the aching tooth, you must scrape around the aching tooth vigorously, to protect the gums from all sides; then, move it with your fingers or fine pliers little by little until it is properly loosened; then firmly grasp the pliers; and place the patient's head in your grasp between your knees, and hold it firmly so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After, extract the tooth straight without breaking it; and if it does not easily come out, take one of these tools and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and gently grip it with pliers, so that it does not break when gripping it; and you must skillfully work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break it, and leave a part behind, and cause the patient greater pain from the root, worse than the first pain.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be warned that you do not act like the ignorant doctors who, through their haste and boldness, sometimes break the jaw and do not achieve what we have described; but they sometimes cause greater illness due to the roots that remain, or by breaking the jaw, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine, or with vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the area with crushed vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one moves the teeth first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have large members so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of good, strong iron, and they should have teeth for holding the mouth.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, you should put cotton soaked in butter on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then use pliers called "algefri", which the head resembles a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with these pliers, you must expose the flesh all around the root, and apply the instrument called "althali", that is to say, a gouge, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out with this, it is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which the shapes follow:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two blades, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which here is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments should be strong so that they cannot break, and know that there are many instruments like teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master, subtly, finds his instrument by himself, according to what his works and the illness show him, because there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of others; and if you break a bone or other bones, where it might be necessary, look among the instruments, which I have told you, and help yourself with the gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but that it can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for it, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, remove it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in young women, then you must know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or ground: then remove it; and if it is connected with the tooth, then take this instrument, of which this is the form, and it is like a small beak, and let it be of hard tempered steel, pointed at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days, because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, file it with a file like this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which needles are made; and file the tooth little by little over several days gently, so that it does not move so much that it breaks; then finish it flat with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without them falling out, and you have treated them with binding medicines, and it is of no value; then you must bind them with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and put it double between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or several, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the wrapping to the point where you began, and draw your hand subtly and wisely, until it does not move at all; and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, join them, and bind them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, bind it with another thread; so it will remain and serve thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the way of straightening the two healthy teeth, and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and let no one intervene who is not wise and patient, and sometimes one makes a form of a tooth from cow's bone, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and fastens it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the tongue tie
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this tie that comes under the tongue is natural, and one is born with it; or through the accident of a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth, and hold their head firmly, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve tie from the side, until the tongue is separated from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from a healed wound, then use the hook and cut that ligament from the side; and be careful that the cut is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done it, wash the area with rosewater and honey, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and the patient must keep it there every night, so the area cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if a bleeding occurs, put powdered vitriol on the area; and if the blood flows, cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a foul colour, or black, or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is tending to whiteness, and there is moisture, then use a lancet and cut it with a small spatula, and remove it from one side and the other; and if the blood flows during your work, then put powdered vitriol on it until it stops, then return to your work until you have extracted all of it; then wash the area with honey and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils appear in the throat, called "godath," and are properly called the two tonsils.  And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if they are hard abscesses, with a small opening and foul colour, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will burst on its own; and if it is white and the root is small, prepare your instrument for cutting, but first make sure the abscess is warm and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, with their head in your care, and open their mouth, and the surgeon should take it between their hands, and press the tongue down with the entire instrument, of which this is the shape; and let it be of silver or fine bronze, like a small knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and insert it into the tonsil, and pull firmly upwards as much as you can; and pull out any matter with it, then cut it with the instrument, of which this is the shape, that resembles a pair of shears; and the points are bent and one against the other, and very sharp, and made of tempered iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cut it with pliers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp, and the other not; and when you have cut one tonsil, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, the patient should gargle with hot water, warm and easy to drink, and if bleeding occurs, the patient should gargle with water, or with boiled pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, then cut them similarly to the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed in her throat, that is to say, a small, sensitive abscess; and it had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so large that it had forcefully pushed two ribs through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly acted, and inserted a hook into one nostril, then pulled it out, and extracted a large portion of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the hook into these abscesses, and cut away a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the space I had emptied, until it became very large; then I cauterized it inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow; and I left this area, and do not know what God did to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When mucus flows down to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen below, round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have described in the division, and the treatment does not work, and you see that the inflamed abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you must cut it; and the one that is round, collected, and not long; and it is bloody or of a dark color or black, then you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said, by its whiteness and length, you must have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention before; then insert the hook into the eye, and draw it downwards, and cut it using one of the two instruments that I have described in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, you will harm the voice, and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cutting, you must use a method of cauterization to overcome their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp, sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head in your own, and then press their tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the cautery chapter, and cauterize with a hot, sharp iron, so that it is neither too thick nor too bright; and apply the end of this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there should be a receptacle on the head, where medicine is placed, like the bowl of a spoon, and place the instrument, with all the medicine, on the ulcer; and let the patient lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth to the medicine, so it does not descend into the throat and injure it; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the ulcer for the length of half an hour, until you see it healed and the medicine's burning sensation is gone; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument, with the cotton, on the affected area until the cotton dries on the ulcer; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the medicinal cautery, reapply it, and after the cautery, wipe around the ulcer with cotton dipped in butter, and clean the area around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is more effective than incision, or than cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamus, ysop, origanum, rue, chamomile, and avron, and similar herbs, and put them all or some of them in a pot, and add water, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument shaped as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or brass, and one of its ends should be placed in the patient's mouth, so that the vapor rises to the ulcer through the pipe, until the ulcer is dead; then repeat it often, until the ulcer dries; and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because many things happen; and only do this when the hot abscess is subsiding.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a pipe and put the end of an egg shell inside, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the egg shell does not allow the vapor to burn the mouth, and this is a good and safe treatment.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times bone or fish spines, or some other object, lodge in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the instrument, so that you can move the object; and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out with the vomit; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it gets to the place, it will dry out, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take a lead instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and the patient's head should be raised; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that it does not swell, nor push the bone inward; it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, so that the location of the object is known; if it is pushed down, or pulled out with the instrument equally, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the leech in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the leech is treated, as I have said in the division, by medical treatment; and when this is not helpful, then look into the patient's throat with the instrument I have described, and press the patient's tongue with it.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine pliers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a thin cord, and put it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the cord, and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is feverish every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the patient's mouth, and pour it in without letting them swallow, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the leech senses the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot containing burning coals, and place a lid pierced in the middle over the pot, and through that hole, place the end of the instrument; then place your fumigation there, and the patient should put the end of the cord in their mouth, and close their mouth, so that no smoke escapes, but reaches the leech; and the leech will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to leave forcefully by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which the leech is pulled is, when it can be seen, like curved tongs to enter into the throat; and it resembles the beak of a bird, and there is a roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many are the types of abscess, according to what the memory brings here after from one and another in this book, and they differ in their perforation and incision; and there are two types, one in its own appearance, and of what moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is according to the locations where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy areas are different from those that arise in the joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is ripe according to its completion; and there are some that must be pierced when they are ripe, and do not mature according to their completion, such as abscesses beside joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes beside joints, and one leaves it until it is rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is next to the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the main limb; or if it is next to the foundation, it is pierced before it is ripe; and you should not pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for one next to the foundation, lest it rot deeply, extend inside, and become a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for the perforation of a ripe abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is calmed, and the fever subsides, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the settling and sharpening of the abscess head, and the other signs; and you must place the perforation in the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and the perforation should be along the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places alike where there is no skin.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy area, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of its poison will extend, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and depth will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And some abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must make small perforations in small abscesses; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where you must cut the core, and cut; when it has become like a flap, and is subdued, you must do as one does with buboes; and there are some that are cut into three angles, and there are some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the groin; and there are some where you make a circular cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those without a head, like a superficial, soft abscess, must be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a large swelling, and you pierce it, you should not extract all the swelling at once, but extract a portion; then stop the abscess until the next day, and then extract some more; do this repeatedly, gradually, until all the swelling comes out; especially if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or young children, or decrepit old men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes jumps with the discharge of the swelling, so that the patient may die, and you are not aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound and examine if the opening of the abscess is small; and if it is a simple incision, apply linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is a large abscess, and it has many perforations, you must place a bandage in each one so that they meet each other; and if you have cut a portion of skin in the abscess, and you have cut around it, you must fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if a discharge of blood occurs during your work, apply cold water and cloths, and moisten a cloth, and apply it repeatedly to the bleeding area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding continues, apply remedies and treatments, and the powders I have mentioned in the appropriate places in this book, and if it is during winter, and the area where the abscess is is very sensitive, you must apply bandages and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, you must apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, dry it and treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must universally know in treating abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head's skin is affected, small abscesses appear, and some are like webs, just like the membrane of a chicken egg, and many similar ones are present.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are greasy and contain moisture like pus; and some are hard and stony when cut, and there is no doubt if the arteries do not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cutting is that you test with every instrument that is called "entromissoire", of which the form comes afterwards, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then it is lanced from above, lengthwise.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, then it is scorched, leaving nothing of the skin containing that moisture, for it often returns when anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; otherwise, in vinegar and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and this will drain what is left from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know for sure that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains fatty tissue, cut it lengthwise along this shape; and insert your probes, and scorch it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to remove the pus where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I have told you later.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And likewise do with the stony abscess, and in cutting and treating it, as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting on a stony and moist abscess is easier, for they are composed of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses, in the head, have no moisture, and such was the abscess that I cut in the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken; and if one had struck it, one would have made a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come in the head, except those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the most dependent place, in order to drain the pus; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses appear on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come elsewhere on the body, and are large, and are clustered together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous swelling is properly within its own cavity, like the cold and the abscess in the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see to have a good disposition when touched, and are of the same colour as the body, and move on all sides and are not attached to the neck nerves, or artery or conduit, and are not deep; you should cut them open from above, and scrape them from every part, and spread the two lips of the wound with forceps if you need, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and drain them gradually, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and let the instrument not be too sharp or cutting, so that your hand does not slip, and do not go too far, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this prevents you from working, put powdered vitriol or other blood-stopping powders on the wound, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you complete it; then use your index finger to see if any small boils remain, and cut and drain them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the boil, you should not cut the boil at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off without harming it; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire boil, you should bring together the two edges of the wound and stitch them now, since there is no excess remaining due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	You must then attend to cutting the root of it, and pulling it out, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those boils that have excess, pierce them where they appear ripe; and pierce them as the previously mentioned one, depending on that, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with an ointment promoting flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrofula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the throat's incision; but I have never seen anyone in our land perform it, and that is the written record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with scrofula, it is necessary that the throat's incision, called "epiglottis," be avoided; and no help should be given by this, because all the veins and the body of the sick person are affected by those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the airway, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it beneath three or four small circles, a small incision across, between the two circles or by the amount of the incision of the surface, not into the cartilage; and that place is suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are far from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, he should stretch the skin of the throat to the whole incision, then cut the skin until he reaches the airway; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said; and this is shown by the discharge of phlegm from the airway that leaps out through the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed where strangulation is feared, bring together the two edges of the wound in the skin, and sew it together alone, without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breathing fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then the epiglottis is cut so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a lady take a knife and stab it into her throat, and cut part of the airways in her windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had flowed from it, and I recognized that she had not cut a vein or artery except the throat, and air was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the lady except that she was hoarse, and she returned to her condition; therefore I say that there should be no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess, yellow in color, and it is often found in women; and it is of two types: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental ones are of two types, one resembling fat masses, and the other like abscesses arising from arterial inflammation; and there is cause for concern, and one should not use strong treatments except for those that are small, and investigate and examine thoroughly: if you find it like a fatty mass, and it is not connected to any vein, cut it as one cuts fatty tissues, and remove all of its covering, if any; and thoroughly investigate everything, and treat it appropriately until it is completely healed.
des nous	of the masses/tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many types of masses exist, of which I will describe all the appearances; and now it is necessary for me to explain all the differences between a mass and a discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is accompanied by heat and fever until the boiling has passed, and the decay is complete; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a mass, there is no heat, fever, or pain; and it contains a surface, which is its own sac, and is the same color as the body, and begins like a blister, and grows larger; and they are of two appearances, either fatty or moist, and many colors are like I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treating the mass, to first examine it with all the tools called "entroussoirs," according to the form it takes in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses of masses is that you take the most moist area you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then in accordance with the size of the abscess; then remove the instrument, and be careful that nothing should be missed.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running moisture flows, whatever color it may be, treat it as I have described for other abscesses; and if, after using the instrument, no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then cut it in a cross shape, and use tweezers to lightly scrape it from each side and be careful to remove the skin where the mass lies so that you can remove it completely along with the mass; and if you cannot remove it completely, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the mass will return many times; and if a little remains, and the blood bothers you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, constrict the wound, and apply soothing hot poultices, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the mass is large, cut the two edges of the wound, and treat it with something that generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the throbbing vein is contrary or otherwise, hasten and fill the area with crushed vitriol, and leave it for two or three days, until the wound begins to rot and the boiling of blood subsides; then return to removing what remains of the mass.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of probing instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and of these there are three that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and of these there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to search for fistulous abscesses; and they are like the needles with which one sews sores, and are made of yellow bronze, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are preferable, and those made of dark lead are more proven for searching fistulous abscesses; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of forceps are of many appearances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are forceps with two curves of three kinds as well; and there are forceps with three curves, and also of three kinds; and there are forceps with two curves, and forceps with only one curve, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments with which one cuts is sharp, and some do not cut much more than on one side, with which one scrapes off the masses, so that one does not cut the vein or nerve; and of these probes are the lancets fitted into handles, so that the patient does not perceive them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, and in abscesses, and in similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the peels of figs, in this shape, with which one stops the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the area that is healthy around cuts of veins, and arteries, and sometimes they are made according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it should be done according to this shape from this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape away the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that generates flesh, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast droops, and is softened by its size as happens in women, then cut it into two sections above, by two similar cuts; so that one is joined to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape off the skin between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply to it what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it gnaws away the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are a type of hard scrofulous swelling, or there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and cure with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofulous swellings, cut it as we have said in the description of scrofulous swellings, and if the wound discharges pus, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is closed over it, abscesses often result, and the same happens with a swollen vein and abscess.  And if one recognizes it as being due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tightening. And if it is due to the vein, swollen areas are clearly visible. And it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, or the elbows, or the neck, or in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
