It is necessary then to avoid iron treatment, and the person in charge should also avoid it, and in those cases where the swelling is from an artery, cut through the skin lengthwise; then open the wound with lancets, and carefully separate the artery from the surrounding tissues until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath, and pierce it through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then prick the area between the two ligatures with a cauterizing agent until the blood within is released, and the abscess is drained; then apply a treatment that will draw out pus, until the wound is closed; then treat it with a suitable ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is from a cut in a vein, you should hold in your hand the part of the abscess that extends to the skin, then insert the needle under the part you are holding, and pierce it, and place a double thread there, so that you pull it through to the other side; then tie the abscess, as I told you, using the ligature on one of the two sides of the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then re-insert another needle through the thread under the entire abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess fluid comes out, then remove the excess from the heart and leave the tied portion; then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply healing poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in the artery and vein, abscesses occur in the nerves when they are injured, or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and fingers, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color resembles the body's color, and is in various painful conditions; and when it is pressed forcefully, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves easily in all directions, and neither forward nor backward, nor below nor above, and those that are in joints should not be cut with an iron instrument; possibly causing a contraction; and those on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, scrape it with a lancet, and remove it, then stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes these appear in the abdomen and nowhere else, and is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance, and its root is subtle, and the head large; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were often cracked, and moisture ran from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found in one eighteen ounces in weight, and in the other six, and the procedure for the incision is that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the swelling is white and moist and of fine roots; then cut it with a wide spatula, and have the fire cautery ready.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the process of cutting, there is often too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overwhelms you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with iron, take a well-made lead thread and tie the swelling with it as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not cease tightening the lead thread until it cuts the swelling and breaks through it without difficulty; and if the roots are large, there is a fear of cutting, especially in the belly, but you can cut half, then cauterize it to prevent it from returning; then treat the wound, and take care not to cut the swelling that is of a fixed color, and poor sense and white appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an entrenched abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is ripe.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a tear in the skin, and is on the belly and some boils come out, as happens in other ruptures, or of blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if it is by the rupture of the skin and the exit of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and appears with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestines, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with one's fingers it recoils, and then returns, and perhaps it is inflamed, and it grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and from hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and appears well when you press it with your hand, and it does not constrain; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess appears large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you should leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and because of the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, you should instruct the patient to hold their breath, and lie stretched out straight, then make a mark all around the affected area; then instruct them to lie often between your hands, then go around the area you marked with all the spatumile, then extend half of the abscess upwards, all the way to the large incisions; then bind it around with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot of the binding be loose; then open half of the extended abscess over the binding, and put your index finger in, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the binding, untie it, and push the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the bowel, take hold of it with the incision, and cut away the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in them, and put the two needles around what you made in a cross that you had pierced; then bind the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you want, remove the needles, and leave the area until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you cut it when it is softened and rotten, then treat it as is necessary, and complete the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as necessary, and suture the area.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the division about the types of ulcers, and how one should treat them with medicine, and how one should avoid iron treatment; and we say that ulcers form in the flesh, and great caution is needed in treatment, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be scraped away, like ulcers on the breasts, and in the thighs, and similar places, one should remove them completely when they are in the beginning; and when they are large and old, one should not approach them, for I have never been able to cure any, nor has anyone ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile sometimes; then make them bleed if they have a manifest fullness, then prepare the patient in a good place to perform the work; then place your incisions on the ulcer, and trim it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe the area well with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding opposes the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed in the division the types of dropsy, how the accumulation of water occurs, the signs of each type, and the treatment using medicine and iron:  only incisions should be considered; and one should not use iron in these two types:  that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, because these are deadly.  Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy called "eclites" with medicine, and the treatment does not help, look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, like diarrhea, vomiting, or similar things; do not use iron, for there is doubt.  And if you see a patient of strong constitution, who has only dropsy and is not too young or too old, you should do the following:  lift the patient up on your hands, and press on their stomach to push the fluid to the lowest part of their body, then take the pointed spatula in this manner:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	and be pointed, yet not so sharp that it can penetrate to the intestines when inserted, and cannot injure them; then look to see if the dropsy is located near the intestines:  then you must make an incision above the navel, three fingers directly below the point of the knife; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the navel three fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, it should be on the right.  And it is not appropriate for the patient to lie on the incision, so the excess fluids do not flow to that weak area; then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand with the entire spatula between the skin and the surface, as if removing a scab with the size of a fingernail or the like; then pierce the surface until the spatula reaches the empty space, and this is the location of the water, then remove it thoroughly.  Then insert this instrument, with the form as follows:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and is of bronze or light-weight metal, and has one small hole on the lower part; and on one side, three holes; and two on another, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision like the writers' cut for the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the head is a valve, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it immediately descends onto the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die due to the dissipation of their vital spirit or faint, or approach death; but empty according to the patient's constitution, and according to the signs of the patient's condition and pulse; then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained due to the seal that stops the hole on the surface, which I have mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the procedure the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and remove a small amount of water; do this several times, and take care not to leave much water remaining.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the patient's condition and leave too much water, treat them with a warm grave or sand bath, by excessive sweating or bathing and in the sun, and make them drink; and treat them with drying remedies until they are cured, and cauterize the stomach, the liver, and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then it must be pierced very subtly in all directions following this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a thin lead plug in the opening, bind it, and keep it this way for three or four days.  When it wants to urinate, remove the plug, allow it to urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it will not be necessary, for the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose opening is small are treated with a lead plug, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are harmed, for some are born with the opening at the top of the penis, so that they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the fluid cannot reach the outlet, and that is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is that the patient lies on their back, then extends the top of the penis and cuts it like the slit of a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should; and be careful of the bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop it with whatever stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Blisters on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters appear on the penis, and it is an unsightly appearance on the flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; you must take them with a fine forceps, cut and remove them all, then apply moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the blister is malignant, with a foul color and odor, you must apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the blister is on the surface of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, you must remove the blister that is inside first; and when it is closed, treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, the penis is not completely sure that it will not be pierced, and there will be blackness and corruption in its flesh and in the scrotum; you must remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply the plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranate and vetches, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood oozing occurs, apply lunar cautery according to this method:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two conditions together: namely, blood flow and corruption; and if the flesh of the penis is corrupted and withdrawn, you should insert a lead tube into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin is affected at the head of the penis, which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a sharp instrument until the binding is loosened, and the flesh of the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is a difficult matter to separate it, you must scrape it with a spatula slightly at the head of the penis and the skin; then gently separate it in two, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water, so it does not burn again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely the separation of tissue like other wounds; however, when we perform this procedure voluntarily, and especially on children, it is necessary that we perform the best and least painful procedure for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not prescribe circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and lords who performed circumcision using a knife, or force, or a scalpel; the heart would flee, for there are two layers, and perhaps one is cut through while the other is left below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	So, it is necessary to cut again, and the pain is doubled, and the cleansing of the foreskin is not ensured, the tip of the member is not. And in the cleansing of the skin, perhaps the iron escapes, and the work is ruined, and many times they are born in such a way that they don't need cleansing, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing done by force, throughout the entire length of the thread, I have found the benefit of experience, for force cuts precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, you cut equally on both sides at the same time; but the thread must be tightly wrapped around the skin.  And the first method should be that you make the child believe, if they understand, that you only tie the thread around the penis. And you can make them happy in any way you can. Then hold it straight between your hands, and apply the force between your hands or under your feet so the child does not see it, or any of the instruments. Then place your hand on the penis and blow into the heart, and pull it upward until the head of the penis is inside; then thoroughly clean it from the dirt that has accumulated there. Then tie the wound with a double thread, then tie it below to another thread. And hold it with two fingers of the second hand on the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two threads, then quickly lift the heart and pull the head of the penis out.  Then allow the blood to drip slowly, for this is the cause of it. And put powder on it and on top of the powder, a diluted egg white mixed with rosewater, and rose oil and fresh oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with further treatments until it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the knife for cleansing is this: the two blades should be sharp and the blade should be as wide as the handle.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing occurs when the heart is inside the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingertip, so the area doesn't become an abscess. And cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingertip, hold it with pliers and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if three days pass, and what is under the penis is swollen, leave it until the hot abscess subsides, and lightly scrape it; cut it as you are able, and be careful of the part of the penis, it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with the powders we described in the section on powders, and if the cut from the heart is excessive and goes upward, it will not harm it; then treat it, as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	About the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we discussed in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention to be due to a stone lodged in the bladder neck, the patient must be bent over their knees, and their feet placed on their back, and their stomach extended toward the back, and the patient must strain as much as possible; and this forces the neck of the bladder to push the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you should use an extraction device called a "syringe," which is shaped like this: it should be made of thin, light silver, like the feather of a bird; and it should be a palm and a half long, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of releasing the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie a small piece of wool or cotton to the end, and place the end of the thread inside the syringe; cut the excess wool and push it to the tip of the syringe, then lubricate the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on a seat, and lubricate the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil and warm water; then gently place the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then pull the penis upwards towards the groin; then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and the patient feels it coming out to the empty space, and this is not always done according to this order because the passage through which it goes is twisted; then pull the thread with the wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow; and repeat the use of the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scabs or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction gathers there, and you see the need to distill liquids and medicines, use a device called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the passage through which the medicine flows should be such that it tightly seals the penis without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push it in when necessary; and when you want to inject your medicines into the bladder, place the tip of the container into the moisture, and pull the inner mechanism; you will draw the moisture into the container, and then forcefully push the mechanism back in; the moisture will enter, and will reach the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the thin enema that is used to irrigate the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or bronze, and the container is higher; and underneath, there is a receptacle into which the liquid flows; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you wish to inject into the bladder in it; tie it between the two receptacles using a strong double thread, and heat a small amount of that moisture over the fire; then place the tip of the enema into the penis; and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a sheep's bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle of it, and pierce it roundly around; then place a strong thread into these holes, assemble the circle as one would assemble a seal, and put inside whatever oil, moisture and water you wish; and place it into the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed the types of stones, and their extraction along with remedies; and I have described the difference between stones formed in the kidneys, and all the symptoms, and in which stones one should perform surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones formed in the bladder happen more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine flows out of the bladder in a thin stream; and it shows grit, and the patient scratches their penis, and it becomes stiff many times, and then softens; and many of these conditions affect the foundations; and the healing is easier in children until they are four years old, and is very difficult in old people, and is moderate in those between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier in those who have large stones than in those who have small stones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the waste from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes appears from the upper part; then have them sit between your hands, with their hands under their thighs, so that the bladder is completely sloping downwards; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then quickly proceed to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall out upon touching it entirely, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is a grown youth; and insert it into their groin, and search for the stone; and when you feel it on your finger, draw it towards the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it outwards where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards towards the nipples, and with his left hand remove the skin underneath the nipples in the area where the incision is to be made; then insert the cutting spatulate, whose shape is this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between that which is between the nipples and the groin, not in the middle but along the side of the left groin; and let it be straight over the stone, and your fingers be near the groin, and let the cut be tapered so that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, and not too large; perhaps the pressure of your finger in the groin will cause it to jump out without effort; and know that there are stones that have angles and edges: these are difficult to remove; and there are some that are smooth, resembling a ball, and round, and easily removed.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must use pincers, like a file at the tip, to hold the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert a thin, curved instrument under it; and if you cannot remove it this way, enlarge the opening a little, and if the blood flows, stop it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first remove the largest to the neck of the bladder, then cut over it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones after if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be slowly removed, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out continuously through the opening because the wound cannot close; however, try to remove it, or break it with pliers, until you remove it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and compress it, and place a damp cloth in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then place the patient on his back, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, thoroughly wash the area with oil and water, then treat it with diachylon and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses, corrosion, and blood clots form in the bladder, and the urine is retained as a result, and blood is seen mixed with the urine: then insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder; then wash the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help him in every way that you can until he is healed; and you must, every time you treat him, tie his legs together and gather the medicines at the location.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out; treat it as I said before, cutting it many times; the cutting is excused by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod according to this shape and let it have three angles stuck into a [piece of wood] in a fork.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then gently insert the rod into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come out immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is immediately broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the urethra at the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will reveal the secrets, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the woman's stone is deeper than the man's stone, because it requires a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity demands this, you must take a knowledgeable woman, and she is hardly found, and if you do not find one, seek a discreet, chaste woman; and present a wise and experienced woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to do what you command her regarding the investigation of the stone; and observe carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must put her finger into the foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must hold it under her finger, and advise her to put her finger where the ailment is and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh near the middle of the opening, where it is most apparent, and feel for the stone in that area; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then widen the incision if you feel the stone, until the stone can be pulled out, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with veins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	So recognize the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overcomes you, apply powdered vitriol, and hold it for an hour until the blood is stopped; then return to your work until the stone is removed, and have the instruments I told you about for removing stones in men to help you in your work; and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the cut artery, put the powder on the area and bind it with bandages and do not resume this, and leave the stone and do not remove it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the area is healed, return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white substance, which is under the skin of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "white substance", and sometimes is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white substance we have mentioned; and this only occurs in a few.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: either it is a color leaning towards jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is in the white substance we have mentioned, it is a hidden abscess, a little long, like the shape of an egg, and the testicles are not visible, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the membrane itself, it is a hidden abscess with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white substance, one feels it well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you should test it throughout the entire area, the shape of which is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, then, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their ability and the fullness of their body; then support them on their back, on something a little high, and put many cloths underneath them; then sit on their left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the heart of the testicles; then take the sharp-pointed instrument, and cut the skin of the testicles across their length, next to the blade, and make your incision straight, dividing the skin of the testicles down to the white substance, and gently peel it back according to your ability; then pierce the white substance full of water with a large opening, and drain all the water, and then put your forceps, and stretch the white substance upwards; and do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the white substance; cut all or in pieces, even the side of it subtly, for if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the white substance; then stitch the two edges of the heart of the testicles together with a stitch, then treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, you must tie the vessels that support it, fearing the escape of blood; then cut the testicle along with the support, remove the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if water has collected in two parts together, know that these are two branches; cut the other part as you did the first, equally, then wipe the blood, and put moistened wool in rose oil in the wound; and put another moistened wool in wine and oil over the two testicles, and put folded cloths over it, and bind it tightly to the whole bandage in this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and fill them with wool according to this pattern, and they should be sewn together at the waistband of the breeches, and one of the ends should be placed over the buttocks to the back, and the other to the area around the blade; and the other two ends over the two armpits, and the entire binding should be fastened to the buckle of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is treated with a cautery instead of an iron incision, in that you should take a subtle scalpel cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white membrane containing the water is exposed; then take the cautery in this manner, and pierce the said membrane with the forceps, and gently peel it with this heated and subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in every way you can, until you have removed everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and be aware of blood loss, and avoid the work of incision; and if anything opposes you, or a boil or blood loss or anything else, treat what opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this operation because of its horror, then perform a perforation, as I tell you, and this is that when you are certain through the signs we have discussed that the watery branch is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part through the entire fleshy area, placing the perforation along the body's length; and let the opening be wide, so that all the water runs freely; then place cotton on the area and bind it, and allow the remaining water to drain, and treat it until the wound is healed; and if the linen bandage does not allow the water to exit through the opening of the wound, you must place a reed or the instrument used to draw water from the dropsical patients, whose form is described earlier; and enlarge the wound slightly, and know that the water returns and gathers again after six months or thereafter, and when it gathers as before, the patient will thus pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the operation and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses arise in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say, due to an excess of water and heat, which spreads to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not have any pain, and is a serious abscess; and perhaps some serious abscesses are fearful and stony, and of a fixed color, and sometimes it comes from the rupture of an artery, or from the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to the rupture of an artery, it is recognized by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	The one made of vein swelling is recognized by its disposition to the pressure of the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this appearance, and on the other flesh; and it is that you cut the skin of the testicles, then lift the testicle upwards, and pull the white membrane away, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all sides of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the testicle is already swollen with its surrounding flesh, then you must pull the testicle and cut it; and if there is air on the surface, or in that which is within the vessels, you must release all that membrane, and cut it smoothly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the flesh is in the rear, you must cut it all and remove the testicle, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enclosed by a wrapping resembling a boil, with softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he moves; and the cure for this disease is almost as dangerous as the previous one, and nonetheless, we will tell you the method, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must have the patient sit on a raised seat, then lower the suspensory of the testicles, down to your fingers, encompassing all the vessels near the penis, and the masters should grasp them tightly, and stretch them fully; then, with a sharp, wide scalpel, cut through the area over the vessels, until they are exposed, and then cauterize each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert a needle with a double thread, and tie it to the first spot where the pus has come out, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, along the length of the body, and remove the corrupted pus; then treat the wound as with other boils, ensuring no vessels that nourish either testicle are cut; for by this, no harm will come to it, and if pus is present on all the vessels, you must remove the testicles from all the vessels so the organ doesn't lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the scrotum.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	This ailment occurs through a tear in the scrotum, or through stretching in the groin area, causing the intestines to descend through the tear into one of the testicles; and this rupture is either of the scrotum itself, or of its stretching, and these two types arise from many causes: from a blow, or a fall, or a strain, or the lifting of heavy objects, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the stretching of the scrotum are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even right down to the bottom, because the scrotum presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign when it is from a cut in the scrotum is that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears differently, beneath the skin, close to the surface, because of the emergence of the intestine and the body pushing through the scrotum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the scrotum, and are retained inside, causing the patient great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments, there is fear of iron, so it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of treatment is that you instruct the patient to push the intestine back into the wound with your hand, if it can be returned; then hold it on his/her neck between your hands, and raise the thighs; then stretch the groin upward, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert forceps into the groin according to your need to open the wound and make it wide enough for the intestines to come out; then scrape the scrotum beneath the skin of the testicles until the hard white scrotum is exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into what lies behind the testicle, between the white scrotum underneath the skin of the testicle and the second layer; and separate what's behind the testicle and between the second layer of the scrotum; then move your right hand inside the groin and stretch the white scrotum upward with your left hand, and lift the testicle with all the scrotum towards the groin; and instruct the assistant to stretch the testicle upward and loosen what lies behind the ligament; and look with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the hard white scrotum, and if you find anything, put it back in the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and put it on the back part of the scrotum, that is beyond the skin of the testicles; after the groin, then cut the threads' ends so that there are four threads; then tie them one over the other in a cross shape, and tie the scrotum, which we have mentioned, that is under the skin of the testicles, with a strong bandage in two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads, and tie them in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter it, so that a burning abscess does not arise; and put again the bandage according to the first bandage, with two fingers in length; and after these two bandages, leave a scrotum space under the groin of one finger width; and after all the rest, according to the roundness that the testicle has; then cut in the part under the skin of the testicles until the blood runs, and the wound is open, as we said before; then apply wool soaked in oil to the wounds, and apply the bandage we have mentioned.
