Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white scrotum that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, due to fear of blood leakage.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and the bandage is left until it falls off by itself; and if it takes too long to fall off, it should be soaked with hot water, and then apply what we have said, until it falls off; then treat the wound with other treatments until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the matter that is bound to the viscera, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above or slightly below; then cut it in half, and treat the abscess with what opens, until the vessels fall out; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the area opens; and none of the intestines descend into the testicles, and if any do descend, it is little, and returns every hour; and yet if it stays too long in this condition, the wound or the swelling increases until the intestine descends; and this happens because of the extension of the swelling in the groin, as we have said, for it extends, then the area softens and swells and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the area of the ruptured swelling broadly according to the quantity of three fingers; and then remove the swelling that is under the skin, which adheres to it; then take the reed and place it on the visible area of the swelling; and press it deeply into the abdomen, then stitch the two visible areas of the swelling over the top of the reed, and stitch both; then remove the reed, and do not cut the swelling or stretch the testicles or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines; then treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is contained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is milder in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles softens in some men, because the tissues within are softened, and it is visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that the patient be laid on his back, and one cuts the softened skin over the natural skin; then brings the two edges together with a stitch, and if you wish, first stitch the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and the stitches come out.
dou chastrement	Of the castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden by our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is that the scholar should know how to answer when asked, and to know the cure; and the other, because we often need castration of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we use by pulling, we make the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then we grasp them with your hand, until they are restored and you feel them no longer.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For castration by cutting: you must restrain the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle with one cut, once you have properly incised them; and leave a little bit of the skin and the thin skin over the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than that which is done by pulling, because with pulling, perhaps some part of the testicles remains, by which the animal desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism in men is in two ways: one is that between the two testicles there appears, also as the figure of a woman's nature, or there is hair, and sometimes urine comes out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has a penis as if a male's, and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of the man and the woman is that you cut all the added flesh, and treat them as other wounds; in the second type, of men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenting is an added flesh on the natural part, so that it is too unsightly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should scrape the excess tenting with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest there be a flow of blood, then treat it with other cures until it is healed; and there is another flesh that grows at the mouth of the wound, and fills it, and perhaps bursts forth, and is like a scab, and because of this the ancients called it "scab-disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it, just as we said for the tenting, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of the erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the woman's nature is not pierced, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental through illness that has come; or it is by added flesh, or thin or thick skin, and is deep in the wound, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps the having of flowers; and knowledge of this is through observation of the bulge.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is readily apparent, seek it with your fingers or with a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is from thin skin, and it is close to the two lips, hurry and do this: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, legs spread; then spread the two lips wide, until the thin skin is round, and the swelling is open; then take wool, soak it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman lie on her side each day, so it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the skin is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula, resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of new flesh, suspend it with a hook and cut it; and have blood-stopping medicines, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then apply a wide lead strip so the wound cannot heal; and let it be for a long time, and apply a dry linen tent; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when new flesh comes in the wound, it must be cut in this manner, if it is not an encysted abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the encysted abscess in the wound, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when hemorrhoids are old they become ulcerated; and we have already mentioned their types, signs, and I will now describe those which receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and ulcers, when deep within the wound and not apparent upon touch, are not to be treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the opening of the wound, which can be felt, are those which can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold house, then grasp the ulcer with pliers, and cut it at its roots, then apply powders of blood-stopping medicines, such as alum, dragon's blood, and frankincense, and similar things; then place her feet against a wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, gall nuts, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and vinegar, and apply a poultice to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts, without causing wounds; then take wool and soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointments until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hard lump, you must cut it, just as I described cutting the ulcer; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of abscesses of the breast.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the breast, such as ulcers, stony abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to describe in this treatise the hot abscess that arises in the breast, which is not among the abscesses that accumulate pus; and if you wish to know the nature of this condition, observe whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, filled with heat and fever, and if it becomes red, you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not rush to pierce it, but allow it to mature until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a seat, with two small seats where they can lean, and rest on their back, and bring their feet towards the outer parts of the leg; and let their thighs spread out, and place their arms under their knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then support their body towards the right side, and administer the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the breast, the form of which follows.  And when you wish to administer this instrument, you must first insert the rod to know the depth of the breast, so that the part of the instrument that enters does not go deeper than it should and does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, you must cover the depth of the breast with cloth, so that the instrument does not harm them; and it is necessary for them to place the cone of the instrument above it and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and it is lanced gently, it must be cut at the top, at the very center; and when the pus is evacuated, you must place moistened tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil, in the wound. Place the tent deep in the wound, and put clean wool soaked in water or boiled mallows on top of the breast and on the incision; then treat it after two days of the appropriate ointment, until healed; and sometimes the breast and wound are cleaned with an enema of water and honey, and then water or boiled roots of lilies and long-rooted aristolochies; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is reopened in the breast, you must avoid iron cauterization, but treat it as we have described in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	First, it is necessary for the midwife to understand the natural pattern of childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pushing down and desiring to smell the air; then the baby hastens to come out. Then know that this childbirth is according to the natural pattern, and the baby comes out under its head, and the afterbirth with it. And when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the baby comes out quickly; for when it descends with its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the breast is cleaned of its superfluities through good cleansing; and that which comes out otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out on its feet, and the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes out on its belly, or its back, and is turned perhaps on its neck, and in other bad positions; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the positions how one should aid it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out with its head in a natural way, and the woman is laboring hard, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a stool, or have the women hold her; and apply her nature's oil or fenugreek, boiled, and then the midwife should put the small spatula, of which the shape is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the afterbirth, and cut with her fingernail until the moisture which is within escapes; and hold the woman's belly until the baby descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil; then have her take and sneeze by forcing it, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: the baby will then come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, it is necessary that you gently bring them back little by little; and if they cannot enter, have the woman sit on a seat, and raise her feet up; then lower the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when it is lowered; and if the hands cannot enter, and the baby dies, cut the hands with the knife that is mentioned before, and take out the child, and bring them back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's exit on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it must be lifted up; and then turn it gently until it is straight; then take one of the feet and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the thighs, instruct her to hold it, and make her sneeze forcibly; if it jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, turn it gently until it is in its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a mixture of plantain, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all into a paste; and apply this ointment to the woman's parts, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened underneath, apply a compress of myrrh, place it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, make her sneeze, and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her stomach, for the child will now jump out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child onto her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes into this position, the midwife should gently place her hands; then the child should be supported on her neck, with feet hanging down, lying on a bed; and gently bend her hands, then grasp her hands on the abdomen, and remove the pillows underneath, until she is ready for delivery; and if the child does not come out, grasp her feet and gently move them, then move her stomach upward, then push with your hands; and gently draw out the child; and instruct the woman to hold on firmly until the child is delivered.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes out with one hand outstretched
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, have the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie down on a bed, and straighten her legs; then administer the ointment that I have described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; and deliver the child in the natural position, have her sneeze, and instruct her to hold on tightly until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child on its mother's neck, with its hands outstretched, and its face turned toward the mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the midwife hold its hand, then gently turn it, and draw it out gently; and when it is equal, apply the nourishing ointment and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move gently; and when you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and instruct her to hold on tightly; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this manner for the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your fingernail, so that the moisture is emptied; and if the child hangs by its face and neck, cut it from the buttocks, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then place the child inside, until you have put it as it should be, and instruct the woman to hold on tightly several times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the birth of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, except rarely; I know this, that they are multiplied, and are separated by the surface that divides them, which is attached to the buttocks; and sometimes they come out just as one whole body, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and do quickly and easily what she does; and do so as it deserves to be done for their safety.
de plusors enfans	Of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more up to fifteen, and are entirely formed in the form of a child according to the measure of the wise and glorious, and the midwife must know all of this, for perhaps such things happen to her; so let her do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to manual work; you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; the woman must be placed on her back, with her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister should support her from two sides, or she should be bound to the bed so that she is not dragged down by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with the muscilaginous mixture of marshmallow, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then the midwife should anoint her hands with these oils and mixtures; then gently put them into the womb, then locate a suitable place to insert the forceps, and watch carefully that the child is positioned so it descends on its head; insert the forceps into its eyes, or neck, or mouth, or palate, or under the chin, or in the groin, or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, insert it into the heels or mid-ribs; and she must hold the forceps in her right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of her left hand, and gently apply it to her whole hand, and insert the forceps into any of these places we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the forceps:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert another forceps, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then extend them equally by moving them to either side, to make it come out, and let the forceps be toothed to hold it, as this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, let the midwife anoint some of her fingers with oil, and put them into that part, and pull the other part; and if any part still remains, place the forceps in a higher position, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back due to the constriction, you must wrap it in a cloth until it all comes out; then cut it at the joint of the sole or with a knife, and similarly you must do with the other hand, and with the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and the passage is narrow, or it has a sharp bone assembled on the head, you must place the sharp spatula between your fingers, and cut the head and remove the bone; or you can use the instrument called "almidach," of which the shape is given with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and do likewise if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it is stuck in the groin, it should be cut open until the moisture that is in the womb comes out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the extraction is gentle, and the straightening at the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or the womb, you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut the belly or the womb until the moisture in it comes out; and if the other members are removed and the head remains, let the midwife put her hand deep into the womb and pull it toward the opening of the womb; then put forceps in and pull it out; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, do not work on it, but apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices and soak it in soft and moist water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, apply what we have said about the living child; and if one cannot do that, pull it out in pieces, and do not leave any of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about hot abscesses that occur in the womb; and if bleeding occurs, it should be placed in astringent water, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had contained a dead child, then another was sewn onto it, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the area, and it swelled until it opened, and began to fester greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I considered it for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong-drawing plaster, and a bone came out, and after a few days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly surprised, because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cleaned the wound, and extracted many bones, until the woman was in better condition; and the woman lived a long time like that, and often a little pus would come from the place; and I have recorded this chapter only so that, when a master finds a strange thing, he may know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here after comes the shape of the press, with which the books were made; and with two turns on the two ends of the two cords.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be 1 finger wide, and the edges of the wood 1 finger, and a palm and a half long; and in the middle of the two cords should be two joints of this same wood, which should be fastened to one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are placed in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and have at its two ends two joints, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the marrow with the entire instrument, have the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging and legs open, then place the two joined joints into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then operate your hand on the whole instrument, as you did with the pliers, in the same manner, according to the quantity you wish to open the mouth of the marrow, so that the marrow does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all surmounted, and their forms are multiplied; and when the master has prepared them, the work is the more hasty, and more highly valued by men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the woman to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with an irritant, and press your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she sneezes because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the marrow, and hold it until vapors come into the marrow; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The afterbirth will be expelled quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out easily, instruct the woman to soak her left hand in oil of sesamum or in marshmallow mucilage, and then place it in the area, and search for the afterbirth; and when she finds it, she should gently and carefully pull it out, so that the womb is not harmed during the extraction; but it should be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled; it will come out and separate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is still constricted, we have described the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not work with all that we have said, be careful not to forcefully pull it out; but it is necessary to tie what is at the mouth of the womb to the woman's thigh, then administer a clyster of four-drug ointment; it will soften and return, and come out easily; however, when it softens, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are necessary for this: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman with retained flowers and afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like a chain, and one places the slender end in the area, and the wider ends above the fire; and let the fumigation be over the embers, and keep burning until it is used up, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but have it stopped up with a thin membrane:  therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and be careful not to touch the ligature; then place moistened wool in wine and oil, and continue the treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it might close up again, place a lead chain in the opening, and leave it there for several days, and remove it when the child is able to use the chamber pot.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these blockages come from the closure of a wound or an abscess; therefore it is necessary to cut through this closure. Then treat it as we described using the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas coming from beneath the fundament are swellings, and those coming from beside the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, can have one or multiple fistulas; and when these swellings are old, they open and discharge whitish or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are piercing; and they are recognized by the fact that either excrement or flatulence comes out when the patient evacuates, and perhaps a worm escapes.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce through to the bladder, and even to the middle of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and the groin.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a piercing fistula from the fundament, and one that is not piercing:  and this is how you do it - put your index finger on the fundament, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula, when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is a twisting, then insert a thin lead tent, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair against your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no excrement, flatulence, or worm comes from the opening, as we have said, know that it does not pierce; hasten to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces to the bladder or the urine duct, urine escapes, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces to the joint of the thigh, the tent reaches the place; if there is no twisting and the pain is around the opening, it often bursts, and no medicine or ointment will heal it; in these piercing fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and the foolishness of meddling charlatans.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not piercing and are not ancient, there is hope for health through iron, as I have proven, and this is how you do it: the patient lies on their back in your hands; raise their legs up to their thighs, and have their thighs inclined to their belly; then insert a tent of bronze or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the fundament, you should insert your index finger; if you then feel the tent has pierced it, and it is uncovered where you feel the surface or flesh between your finger, then know that it is piercing; do not work on it if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says, however, that some can be cured, but this is rare; and the help one gives is to heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and to place it, hot, in the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that the scorched flesh, which is like a bird's feather, is burnt; and then cure it with moist tents in butter, until the flesh comes out, then cure it with an ointment that will generate flesh and cause healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this, in another way, cannot be healed; and if the tent goes in, but does not pierce to the finger that is on the fundament, and there is a thick layer of flesh or surface between your finger and the tent, and you see the fistula at the beginning of the covering of the wound; cut it at the beginning of the fistula and advance the tent, and then place the cautery, until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then clean the scorched flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood gets in your way, and runs between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cauteries of fire gather two good things: that is to say, the burning of these joined flesh, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then cure it with moist tents in butter or crushed herbs, until the place gives off pus, and the burnt flesh comes out in the pus; then treat the wound with healing ointments that generate strong flesh, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula goes right to the bottom of the fundament, and is far from the body, put your finger in the fundament and explore it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between the two is the tissue or the skin or flesh, or it is close to piercing, there is no stronger way of hope and trust, by the administration of one of these three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it all the way through, or if you can, put tents and treat it as before; and do not go too deep, so that you do not cut the tissue that holds the fundament, and the discharges come out without your desire; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will be cured, or you remove that covering and cleanse it after it is cut near the fundament, either with a tent or another suitable instrument; then cleanse that wounded flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can; then try to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula outside the fundament: it will be a lighter thing for the sick person.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament next to the skin above, take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one twisted thread in two, and put the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing into the margin of the fundament inside, then pull the thread from that hole, as if you put your finger in the fundament; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and tighten one against the other, and leave it one or two days; and tighten it sometimes, until the thread cuts the tissues that are between the two, and they fall out; then treat the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make it cut so deep by the lacing, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile spine, with which one cuts the fistula, is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two types: either they are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and often bleed, and there are one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and often a little yellow water or a little blood, and have the color of the body; and the cure for those that have them within the fundament is that you instruct the patient to strain himself to go to the chambers, so that the fundament lets them out, and the threads appear; hurry, and pinch them with tongs, or hold them with your fingernail, then cut them at their roots; and if the forceps cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder them with some hot powders that are in the place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then treat them with other cures until they are healthy; and if the fundament cannot come out, then enemate the patient with a biting and harsh enema to wash what is in the fundament, so that it can come out openly; when the patient strains, and the threads are outside the fundament, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your fingernail or with tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healthy, and that he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must administer the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread over and pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one to drain the excess blood; then put a cloth soaked in rose oil or ointment on the fundament, and place it on the fundament, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they fall, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointments and other remedies until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the fundament
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of the bowels, and by constriction of nature, and when the patient is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must scrape the scab off with a spatula or your fingernail, which will not allow it to moisten; then treat it until it is healed as necessary; and if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it is very sore and scabby; then treat it until it is healthy.
dou fremit	of the tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small, deceptive appearance around the body, and goes very deep; and sometimes it is found cold, and it is felt just like a tremor, and it comes over the whole body, and more to the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a stick of a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that stick over the tremor, so that the circle encompasses the entire tremor; then turn your hand around the entire stick until you cut around the tremor, and push it deep, and remove the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one from a copper or iron stick, according to this form, and let it be thin underneath and pointed on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Not piercing, so as to hold it on the finger, and press it.  And if you wish, cauterize the tremor, as it is previously described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or gold, or of melted or hammered copper; and sometimes these instruments are made small or large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those, then, that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and sorrowful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there be a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the bottom be pierced; and have on one side two holes, and on the other one; and let the belly, where one puts the medicines, be of an animal's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and have between each hole one inch of space, then put into these holes one strong thread of coarse thread twisted in an X or spiral, and gather the belly as if it were a bag; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the clyster; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or similar substance, then put it in gently; then the administrator squeezes it with both hands together until it is all emptied, then remove the clyster, and the patient raises their legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps soundly all night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer it in a disease of the running belly, and the medicine is quick to come out, then repeat it until it is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster upon which the skin is constricted:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicines, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and the cut of a sword and knife, or of a lance or staff or arrow, or of similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from the throwing of a stone or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless broken and the wound is large, and you fear a hot abscess: then make it bleed immediately with the cephalic, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the injured part; and keep the patient from overfilling on wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to bleed, let his food be lessened, and let him drink no wine, nor eat no meat; and put on the wound, if a hot abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not altered by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the heat has altered it, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by bandages, bring them together by stitching, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the abdomen.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat hearty foods, such as roasted meats and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rot in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, cut away all the rot, and burn it, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, seek out the artery, and if you find it dislodged, tie it with a thread; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light; and it is that you put this powder on, which heals even if the heat has altered it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; living coals three parts, and powder it finely, and fill the wound, and press it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coals alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has not altered the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heat has altered the wound, especially in the state, one does not put this powder on it; but one puts on some prepared ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it creates a scab; then treats it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, one must gently grip it with tweezers; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
