Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs in the neck and it is simple, it is no different from one on the head; but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy than to let the wound heal, and to not put anything constricting on it, because it harms the nerves and causes them to retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is also with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be soft, such as warm water, mixed with rose oil, and cuckoos' eggs washed in sweet water, and other stones of the mine in this way, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch it up and bind it with bandages, then let it heal until it is sound.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is festered and full of pus, pierce it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut and bleeding results, drain it, and bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the conduit is protected, through which the food passes, sew the heart on the lining of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then tighten the closure and leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is sound; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, search for it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all those you can, and those that you cannot, leave them until the wound festers, and the exit is separated and lightened; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle the powder I mentioned on it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, observe if wind escapes from the wound as the patient breathes; know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it because of the blood that does not remain deep and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put an attracting ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three, four, or more days; thus, there will be no spasms, nor tremors, nor constriction of breathing; and when you see good conditions, know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then treat it with bandages and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal and festers, then know there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut with a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it as mentioned before; if it is large, by sewing; and if it is small, by powder; and if it has penetrated bone, and has broken pieces, search the wound and remove them if they are separated; and if they are not separated, let the wound fester, so the extraction will be easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Rupture of the belly is great, medium, and small; from the large wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, causing their penetration; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because it is more difficult to return the intestines, if they are not put back immediately; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, returning more difficultly, and that is why a medium-sized wound is more useful, because it is easier to return the intestines to their place than in the other two. And know that rupture of the belly is according to four types: two common sutures occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body, and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds; and yet they are more specific to the stitching of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, and it is difficult to return it, this is due to one of two reasons: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a cloth in lukewarm water, or boil it in water with vinegar, cypress, and rue, and warm the intestines until the swelling is gone; and sometimes astringent wine is used, and it is better than water alone for de-swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling recede, moisten the intestines with water or cooked elderberries and mallows, for this makes the entry easier with little effort; and if it cannot enter, slightly open the wound with an instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than the cutting, for which no one should cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument for slitting it: cut inward in a curve and not outward, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, return them back to their proper natural place, if you can, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is located below the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on their back, and elevate their legs higher than their head; and if it is below the stomach, elevate the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and if the rupture of the abdomen is in either of the two parts, focus on positioning the injured part higher than the other; and thus, this should be administered in both large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is prepared, then take a soft cloth that covers the entire rupture with one hand, and bring the edges together; and this is the common method of stitching, and is to take a needle, or several, according to the size of the wound, then leave a finger's width from the beginning of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the underlying skin, so that you pierce through both, and bring the two edges of the underlying skin together; then pull a double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring the two edges of the wound together, then leave a finger's width, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do this with as many needles as needed until the whole wound is closed; and the needles should be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter properly: therefore, they should be medium; and you should not push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and widen the wound before it heals; and then cut the ends of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while they sleep, and place a dressing or bandage on the ends of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound heals; and this method of needle stitching is more suitable for small wounds, because one or two needles suffice. The second method of stitching is common, and is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the underlying skin with a needle and strong medium thread; and when you have pierced all four edges together, pull the needle back to the starting point, as one sews cloth; and put a space of the size of a finger between each stitch; this stitching is effective, and I stitched a wound a man had in his stomach, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was over a palm in size, and intestines protruded about two palms, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestines after they had been out for 24 hours, and the wound healed in 15 days, and I treated it, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat it with ointments, because I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines; and I applied old cotton to the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and push it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the skin straight through, take the edge of the underlying skin where you inserted the needle, and pierce it through from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew just as a leatherworker sews leather, and that you leave the underlying skin on one side and pick it up on the other, until the stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen properly described, is like some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and bring one edge of the underlying skin to the other, in this manner: insert a needle into the nearest edge of the wound, and pierce only that spot, and leave the two edges of the underlying skin; then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside to the inside, through the two edges of the underlying skin; then pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside, into two other edges of the wound on the other side; and this is the more subtle and most common method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this, and some testify, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each with thread; and one should insert one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew leather straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitch is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the wound is like the treatment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, before the pus has changed it, you put the intestine back in place and stitch it; then apply a powder of healing herbs, and if the pus has changed it, apply whatever ointment is available until the wound begins to heal; and when the threads come out and the skin and the wound are closed, treat the wound like other wounds until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then as soon as it starts to fester, apply old cotton and change it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound may spread to the main limbs, you should soak light wool in temperate oil, or rose oil, and place it around the ankles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or festering in the joints, and this happens frequently, then irrigate them with warm dark wine, especially if the festering reaches the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when wounded, due to the abundance of veins within it, and due to the delicacy of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon jumps out of the wound, replace it as you would the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned dark or black, you should tie the black area to prevent bleeding, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the tie, and hang the two ends down from below the wound to the outside to ease the extraction when the tendon falls and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became a fistula, and there came out the excretion and the flatulence; I treated it according to what I could, and I did not cease to refine my treatment until it was healed, and the area was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner: take a leech with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the leech has opened its mouth, place it over the two edges, so that it closes its mouth over them; and then cut off its head, and this holds so that it cannot loosen, then put another leech in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and stitch the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These leeches are applied to the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and the intestine can be bound with a fine thread, cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this intestinal thread, which is very lean, and then tie to the end of this thread a thread of fine twisted linen, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and bring it together in the rupture; and this manner of leeching is no more than according to the way of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the large intestines, there is no skill nor remedy but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes chronic, is universally called "fistula," especially when it is festering and discharging pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula, in truth, is a hard, white, ulcerated swelling where there is no pain, and is as festering as the feather of a bird; and sometimes clear pus oozes out, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times quite a bit; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is only by one of the eight causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or body; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, that does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the area is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the digestion and healing are slow in the region, and it swells by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to make you aware of the treatment of fistula that is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that arise from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or in some joint of the hands or feet; and there are some that affect the properties of the principal limb, and similar locations.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this type are difficult to heal, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I have mentioned, and you are confident in the cure, and want to know it, take a tin or iron probe, if the fistula is straight, search with it; and if the fistula is crooked, search it with a thin lead probe, because lead bends easily around the curves; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot easily probe it with probes, flush it through one of the openings, for the moisture will flow from one opening to another, and clean it; then search carefully as best you can, to know if there is bone or nerve, and is festering deep, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressing your hand, and the place where they feel it; and when you truly know the location where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, cut it according to what I have said, and remove forcefully the ulceration and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then place softened probes soaked in sharp medicine, and insert them to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments to the new flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the main limb, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all the corruption is removed, then treat it with things that produce new flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and pus returns as before, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small piece of corrupted bone that you can remove with pliers, remove it with a suitable instrument; and if there are many bones, remove them all, leaving none; and if the moisture causes difficulty, and there is no error or fear, cut the moisture and flesh, and expose the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, place something on the wound to cause decay, and leave it until the area around the bones is decayed, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, remove only the corruption until the blackness is all gone, then restore the wound; and if a large part of the corrupted bone reaches the marrow of the bone, it must be scraped and cut all the way to the corruption, and then treated until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that originated within the body, so that the matter reached the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no valid reason to avoid opening it; but the doctors in their foolishness worked so hard that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and became a fistula, and many openings appeared that all emitted pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors applied treatments for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and the large amounts of matter flowing through the openings; and the young man's skin turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one was connected to another throughout all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the openings until I uncovered part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached the bone inside; I scraped what appeared of the corrupted bone, and thought there was no further corruption, other than what I removed; and I began to restore the wound with healing medicines for a long time, and it could not heal; and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and scraped it, and then removed it, and I tried to heal the area; but I couldn't until I cut around a palm's breadth of the bone, and removed it completely to its marrow, then restored it with medicines; and it was healed and healed quickly, and it did not need to start the work again, except for the weakness of the sick person, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation, he often gasped, but he was completely healed, and a hard flesh grew in place of the bone, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction at all, nor in the air nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be scraped in this way: take one bandage, and bind it to the head of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to extend it upwards; and place another bandage of wool thicker than the first bandage, and bind it over the flesh that is over the bone, and extend the head so that you pull the corrupted flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh above the area where you want to scrape, so that the scraping does not hurt the flesh; and place a cinder or a board under the bone to help cut the corrupted flesh; and one must scrape as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and scrape again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not show, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a cinder underneath, and then scrape from one part to the other the corruption, and let the scraping be the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and scrape the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is in the nail of the hand, or in the nail of the foot, that thing is very severe, but nevertheless you must inquire into that corrosion, how it appears to you; and clean it in all the ways you can, but that the vein or nerve does not oppose you; and know that the instruments and scrapers for cutting these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their thinness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this, it is necessary to prepare a tool for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the types of diseases; so consider the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder might rot either due to internal causes, or due to external causes; and when you have treated that corrosion with medicine, and it does not work, then you must cut that limb down to the place where the corrosion is, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater harm of the limb's defect; and the signs are that the limb turns black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and then rots after the blackness, and then the corruption of the limb spreads to other limbs, and affects the whole body; so hurry with the cutting, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creatures, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corruption is at the tip of the finger, cut it off and do not give it time to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no amount of treatment has the power to cure it; and do the same when the corrosion reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut it after the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot; and if it rises to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it goes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the way to cut or scrape the limb is that you bind it above and below, and have some assistants pull one of the bandages down, and others pull the other bandage up, and you separate the flesh between the two bandages to a width of a span, until the bone is exposed; then cut or scrape it, and place a linen bandage on each side, so that the scraping does not touch the healthy area, and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while you are working, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some astringent powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: a blackness appeared that resembled a burn, and that corrosion first appeared in his toe of his foot, until it affected his entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cut off his foot, and was healed; and a long time later, the corrosion returned to the finger of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied repelling substances after cleaning his body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, as I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because his vitality was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and hurried to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have only recounted this so that others may do likewise, if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess occurs in a fleshy area, and it lasts so long that it gathers a large amount of pus; then it bursts and the pus escapes, and the area remains empty, like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a delicate cloth, and it does not extend to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deep within, it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut the skin all around, especially when it is thin, like a cloth; and it will not spread because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you suspect that the skin is inflamed, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with a clyster in this way: examine if the abscess is large, and the pus emanating from it has a foul odor, then clysterize it with Egyptian medicine, which is made like this: take honey, oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and put them in a vessel over a fire until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of this, according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize the abscess, and constrict the opening; and leave the medicine in for two hours, then extract it by pressing; do this repeatedly until the abscess is cleansed and the foul odor is removed; and sometimes clysterize with ash water, when this medicine is not available, and you take vine wood ashes, and pour water over them, then strain it, and use it for a clyster, until you are sure that the abscess is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate Egyptian medicine or ash water, then clysterize it with water and honey, or add a little ground litharge; or you can clysterize with honey and diluted wine, because honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and wine helps to heal the abscess; and when you have done this and you believe the abscess is well cleansed, then clysterize it with something that promotes flesh growth, such as a diafinit plaster, mixed with rose oil and wine; or clysterize it with some of the ointments and medicines, of which I have described the properties in the section on ointments; and if the opening of the abscess is small and the clyster tube cannot enter, widen it a little with an instrument, and insert a tent of Egyptian or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, cut it down to a small area where the clyster can be inserted, and if the pus-releasing opening is on top, cut it or the lowest possible opening.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the abscess from below as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the pus flows to the lowest point, for when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the abscess from below as you wish, prepare it in this way: so that the pus flows easily downward, and nothing of the pus is left behind; and take consolidative medicines to put on the abscess, and place a linen cloth over the entire abscess; then cut a little wider space around the abscess opening than the first, then apply a soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the abscess opening to help release the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except once after several days; and the one that is over the abscess opening, remove it often to remove the pus, and understand if what comes out of the pus is venom, little or much, digestible or indigestible; and be aware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not; and when your medicine has been applied in this way and you see the nature of what flows out of the abscess opening, understand that the abscess is healing, and healing is approaching; and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the abscess discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the abscess will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom flows out after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For some people experience slow flesh regeneration in their wounds, and others experience the opposite; and if undigested pus flows from the abscess after many days, know that the abscess will not heal; and if the abscess is slow to heal and is prolonged, add drying medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diafinit ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take diafinit ointment, and mix it with rose oil and diluted old wine in equal parts; then refine and use it; and the same can be done with honey, cooked and thickened, when diafinit ointment is unavailable, or you can take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense, and grind them into powder, and sprinkle them on the honey while it's over the fire; and then apply it to a cloth, and apply it to the abscess; and sometimes a long-rooted aristolochia and roots of the celestial lily, which is similar to the flour of vetch and centaury, are used; and use them in simple or compound form: grind them, make them into powder, and add them to the honey I mentioned, and use them; and if the treatment is prolonged and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and has pressed into the bone, or hard parts, or ligaments; treat it using the fistulous treatment, as we have described before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaricium is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or perhaps in other digits; and when it is old and not cared for, it develops into a painful abscess, and it flows and expels pus, running along the root of the nail, and perhaps running along the entire nail; and the infection reaches the bone, causing foul pain, and the finger becomes swollen, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we described in the division, and the treatment does not work, you must cut away all the excess remaining nail with a sharp knife, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is very helpful if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and starts to prick and injure it, you should place a blunt instrument under the nail that is pricking the flesh, and lift it, and carefully and gently cut the affected flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines to the remaining flesh to remove it entirely; then treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the infection is in the bone, cut it out and remove it completely, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the finger is corrupted, cut it off as previously described, then treat it until it heals; and if it is injured, and pushed in, and it feels intense pain, you must heal it first; then cut the nail of the affected part with a sharp knife by cutting across the top, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would experience excessive pain; and if it does happen, put something on it that soothes it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the finger's tip.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The extra fingers that sometimes appear on people's hands are sometimes entirely fleshy, sometimes have bones, and sometimes a nail.  Some of them grow at the base of the joint, or in unusual places on the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that grow from an unusual part of the finger do not move, and those that grow at the joint of the finger sometimes do move; the cut of the fleshy one is gentle in this manner: cut it at its root with a wide knife.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the base of the joint are difficult to cure: avoid cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those that grow on the finger's back, you must first cut the round flesh down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable knife, and then treat it until healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining together of the fingers comes from growth, or from the healing of a wound, or from a burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut the joining, so that the fingers return to their natural forms; then place between them soaked cloths or oiled bandages, so they do not rejoin; or you place between them thin pieces of lead until the place is joined, as is appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a joining occurs between any of the fingers and the palm, cut that joining as is appropriate.
des vils	of the wicked/vile/low people
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Large, swollen veins, full of melancholic superfluities, that come in many parts of the body; and more often occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must give him a purge of phlegm, and then heal him with basilikon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is that they cut it and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure is as follows: first, the leg is soaked in very hot water until the thick blood is thinned, then the leg of the sick person is tightly bandaged from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, or two, or three places, with a wide incision, then raise and draw the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows as the patient's strength can tolerate; and then bandage it, and tell him to eat foods that produce black phlegm; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lifting of it is as follows: shave the patient's leg if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and soak the leg in hot water until it turns red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, then cut it along the vein from the top of the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with a knife, and scrape the vein on both sides, until it appears when touched; and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then place the scraper underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then hang it lightly on a hook, then cut it in another place over three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the scraper, as you have done, and hang it on another hook, as you have done before; then make another incision, or several if needed, then lift it and cut it at the toe, then draw and lift it until the second incision; then pull it from incision to incision until it is all drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, then put a strong double-threaded needle, tie it and pull it, and place a scraper underneath, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out; and take care that it does not cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and this brings harm to the patient; and when you have completely drawn it out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted, twisted, and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut straight, so as not to cut the vein; and it is of a large curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be as thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is embedded in legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in land with no moisture; and perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes within the body of serpents and worms, embedded between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head appears, you must wrap around it a piece of lead of one and a half to two ounces, and a bandage, and let the lead hang on the leg, and every time a bit emerges outside, wrap it around the lead and the bandage; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will return into the flesh and cause abscess and rot in the place, and a bad illness; for which reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when treated, is five palms long, or ten, and a man came to me once, from whom it emerged ten palms long, and when you cut it, you make one incision or opening, and pierce it to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and empty the matter that is inside, and apply medicines to the place to stop any rot for a few days, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot or on the foot, and many openings come, and from which it sprouts branches; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called "bull's disease" in our land, because it often happens to bulls, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body, up and down, and one feels it well by the aching of limb to limb, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and bursts out; and it is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, as are worms, serpents, and leeches and ascarides in the belly; and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body and reaches the head, and comes to the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to treat and remove it, you can only remove it when it is visible:  you must then tie the area above and below with a strong bandage tightly, then cut open and pull it out.  If the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies. The greatest harm it does is when it reaches the eye, as we have said. If you see it approaching the eye, press the eyebrow firmly below it, then cut open and pull it out.  The patient should use cleansing remedies for the body and medicines that dissolve bad, putrid humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This ailment is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs, and may move from limb to limb; and I have seen this, as I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and soon after, I saw it rise, like a worm on her shoulder, faster than anything, like quick silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot, and settled in her shoulder, and then a short time later ran throughout her whole body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it frequently circled around her body, just as I saw it do.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb like that, for I had never before seen this ailment in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many cases where pain had moved from one place to another, but I had never seen it like this in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and exposed veins, and because of this the windiness appeared constrained; and it does not appear in this way to those who are well, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.
