And when you wish to cure this ailment, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears as we have described, then you should apply leeches to it above and below quickly, and then cut until that constrained windiness in the area goes away; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, treat it with those remedies which dispel the windiness, such as stinking pills, and seraphin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and feathered ones, and those with heads; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that strikes any limb strikes in two ways: either in a principle part, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes any place on these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: you must avoid the extraction of this arrow, because death follows in many conditions; and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the thin membrane that is over the brain, is, when there is blindness and stupor and paleness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps blood flows from the nostrils, or from the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and from the wound, white moisture like pus, and it also jumps like burning flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then avoid treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were lodged in a hard, not empty, thing; and perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat and fainting come: know then without doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow striking the lung are that frothy blood flows from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and gasps loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the chest, it is beside the small ribs; and expels great phlegm and great pain and gasps; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps some undigested food will flow from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and bits of straw come out through the intestines, there is no hope for treatment, nor for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine flows out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and hips and thighs and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of his nose: I tried it, and drew it out from the other side under the fat of his ear, and he was healed without difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I drew out an arrow that struck the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrow was lodged, and I could only reach the point towards the shaft.  The arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, with a light head without feathers; the patient was healed, and no bad accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic, with feathers. I incised the chin, and worked carefully until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew an arrow from a man, which had lodged in his belly, and I thought he would die. And after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change. I incised over the arrow, and lifted it out, and extracted it completely.  There was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I saw a man whose arrow struck his back, and the wound was closed over it; but the arrow remained inside, and his natural disposition did not change, nor did he experience any adverse natural effects.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, whom an arrow struck in his face, and the wound closed over it; and it remained thus without suffering much pain; and many others similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I drew an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had struck him in the middle of his nose, and it was slightly inclined toward the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat him after it had lodged for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I probed it with a very fine probe, and felt nothing; and he felt a prickling and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the area, so that it wouldn't swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I kept the plaster on for several days, and the wound healed completely again, and the patient remained so for a long time, until he felt the arrow lodged in his nose for one day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied an acute corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it opened up, and probed it, and felt the head of the arrow beginning to emerge; then I continued to apply the acute medicine to the opening of the wound, until the arrowhead became clearly visible; and the process took about four months, and then the wound enlarged so that I could use pincers, and moved it from side to side, and it wouldn't come out; then I didn't stop trying and devising different tools, until I finally, one day, used well-made pincers, according to what their shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it nevertheless, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you apply your treatment to what I have not said, for the book cannot encompass everything; but a wise master, considering a small detail, and what is present and lacking, finds new work, and new tools, for dealing with the strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the members in which they are lodged except in two ways: either through the place where they entered, or from another part; and the one that exits through the place where it entered is an arrow that has entered fleshy parts, and sometimes exits right away.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not exit immediately, leave it until the surrounding flesh has become soft and the exit is eased; and also if it is lodged in bone, and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and move it each day; and then it will exit, and if it does not, pierce around it with a very fine drill, until the surrounding area is widened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the skull bone, and goes down to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the symptoms I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not extract it, but leave it until it is equalized after several days, for if the arrow reaches the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone, and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains for several days without bad symptoms, then attempt to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be removed, apply drills around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in a part of the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the entire wound; and if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, widen the wound until it is large; and extract the arrow if you can, and if there are ear-like protrusions on the arrow by which it is held, remove the flesh that is lodged on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the arrow's ears, so that you can pull it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, as you might pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you hesitate, apply the remedies we have discussed in its chapter; and be careful of cutting into nerves and veins, and devise a way to pull out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the position he was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest aid there is; and if you cannot, then place him according to the signs that show you how.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes out from another part, or if there is anything of it showing, or the skin is swollen in an obvious spot, then cut there, so that the tongs can grasp it, and then pull it out: it will leap out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then resume the extraction until it leaps out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, then grasp the entire shaft; and if the shaft has fallen, and you wish to administer a thrust, then administer an instrument with a point, so that the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument; and then thrust it out, and if the arrow is pointed, then use an instrument with a point entering it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has struck the foot or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, then cut it out; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers with which arrows are extracted is similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird, for pushing at the point of the arrow, just as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and for grasping is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one bleeds, of which there are sixteen in the head, namely: two arteries located behind the ears, called the two "herbech"; and the two arteries that are on the two visible temples; and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two guindeges that are in the neck; and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and is above the fossa, and is the one from which one bleeds, which is clearly visible above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the ulnar and radial, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the bend of the wrist on the left side, and the second is behind the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is on the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Bleeding from the veins behind the ears helps with chronic colds and migraines; and the method of bleeding, as I told you, is that you should raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then the patient should strain their neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head; then grasp them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, it will show; then take the lancet, and place it under the vein towards the bone; then lift your hand upwards with the whole vein, and cut both the skin and the vein with two finger-widths of blade, and make the blood flow as you want; then constrict and bind it until it has stopped bleeding; and I have already discussed incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Bleeding from the two arteries on the temples is good for chronic, severe migraines, and habitual eye inflammation, and for sharp eye pain; and the method of bleeding is as I said:  the patient strains their neck until the two veins appear clearly; feel the pulse under your finger, and then know where the veins are; then lift the head towards the vein with your index finger, and place the lancet underneath, lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done with the other veins, and allow the blood to flow according to your needs; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it stops bleeding; and we have already discussed their incision and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as good as bleeding from the cephalic vein for chronic facial ailments, and for migraines, and for redness; and the method is that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "excavator", of which the shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and strike it with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you want; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it stops bleeding, and sometimes use a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the bandage should not be too sharp; and bandage it transversely, for the bone is close, and perhaps the bandage will break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Bleeding from the two veins in the temples helps the eyes, and for eye inflammation, and redness, and for pus in the eye, and for facial illnesses; and the method of their bleeding is that the patient strains their neck by twisting as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be across, a little longer than the bandage, somewhat wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is thin, perhaps it will break; then let the blood flow as much as you need, and then apply a bandage over the cotton, and tie it tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding from the vein in the nose is good for fever, and for sudden madness, and for facial illnesses, like headaches and redness that appears on the face, especially when it's chronic; and the method of the bleeding is that the patient strains their neck, then presses their nose with your left hand, and take a thin long bandage, and place it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein is not very visible there, and the blood will start to flow; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bandage it for a night, for it heals quickly; and this is the form of the bandage:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Bleeding from the two temples helps with constriction of the urethra, and for the beginning of swelling, and for many illnesses, and for impetigo, and for sores, and for herpes, and for boils; and the method of the bleeding is that the patient strains their neck, both above and below, as we said before; and the master stands over the patient's head, and the patient sits on a stool, then bleed the vein lengthwise, somewhat wide, then draw blood moderately, or as much as needed; then do the same to the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and press both veins moderately, so the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, so the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins on the lips helps with colds in the mouth, and with the corruption of the gums, and cracks in the lips, and the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the method of the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you, and to hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look for the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being dark, and by the fact that there are small dark veins around them: then cut one and the other, and if you don't recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest on each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding from the veins under the tongue helps after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is for constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eyes, and diseases of the mouth; and the method of bleeding is that the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun, and pull their tongue out, and look under each side for a dark vein: bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, for the arteries are underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arms, which are commonly bled, are bled in two ways: either by pricking with a wide, blunt lancet, or with a narrow, pointed one like a surgical knife, and it is called "anesil"; and they are broad or narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the blunt lancet is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is needed to open veins filled with thick, visible blood, and containing thick and troubled blood; and that is the shape of the pointed lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed and narrow, and is for bleeding the thin veins, where there is thin, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, aids in illnesses below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it behooves the bleeder to bleed wisely, and that he beware of the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a bleeding of blood comes, it should be stopped, as I have said; and the lancet should not be pointed, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, you must restrain it and change to another; or you seek another vein, or you bleed the vein in the middle of the arm: it appears clearly; and you cut it with the lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the bleeding site, first you must restrain the arm, touch the site until you feel the pulse; then mark the site with a mark, then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a cutting lancet; and be careful not to wound the artery when you see the site pierced, for it is the artery; dry it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see blood welling up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery: hurry then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it like this, and let the patient not move it; and let him be on guard, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overwhelms you, and the medicine is not present, cut the artery if it appears, for its source retracts; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a fig-tree bark, split it, and take one half and bind it firmly until the next day; if the blood stops, it is good; if not, treat it as we have said, with the powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not difficult in many conditions due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bandage.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the vein in the middle helps to draw blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful about the nerve that is below, and if it pierces too deeply, and it finds the nerve, and it swells and the health is difficult, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its subtlety, you must bleed it with the lancet; and dry the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by puncturing at the olive-colored vein or the myrtle-colored vein, because it is the safest of all the veins, since there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and it is not harmful if you miss the first time, and you start again; and perhaps the place swells in some people when you miss the first time, but it is not harmful.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is only administered to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins on the arm: that is to say, the cephalic, the basilic, and the median cubital; and one should bleed in the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding administered for illnesses has no set time, but only when necessary, by day or by night, at all hours and times; and children should not be bled until fourteen years old, nor women who are pregnant except from the fourth to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people over sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever way, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle clyster, if they have retained much waste, so that the veins do not draw impurities from the intestines that harm the main limbs; nor should one bleed those who are overly full of food, or drunk, as long as they are; nor those who are hydrops; and one should avoid bleeding after colic, vomiting, loose bowels, multiple sexual activity, childbirth, and labor, and extended waking and fasting, and those things which completely deplete the strength, whether of the soul or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thick, by means of food, drink, and medicine, if you have the power; then enter a bath, if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein on the arm near the elbow, as we have said; and guard against work, labor, lust, and similar things that day; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the person being bled, and the bleeder should rub the arm two or three times, then gently tighten the bandage above the middle; for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow; and then the bleeder should rub the area with their hands until the veins swell and are felt; then the bleeder should wet a cloth with a little bit of old oil, then place their left hand over the vein just below the bleeding site, so that the vein does not burst and fail when it is pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like cords when bleeding, and there are those that are full of wind, so that when one places the cloth over it, it recoils, and the vein cannot be opened, and it is the same for those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for this reason, the bleeder must be careful in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, then he should start again a little below or above that place quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let him wait one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps pus will result; nor should he enter a bath, then restart the bleeding if he wishes; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you fear that it will not release as much blood as you want, then press the cloth firmly into the same opening; and open it quickly, before the place swells; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, but place a little oil poultice, for it reduces the body's blood, and the poultice is milder in that place than oil; and thus apply oil poultice in each bleeding you perform on the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this does the same with chalk and wax, when one puts it on the place; it thins the blood and separates it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens often, especially when the bleeding is not strong the first time or when the opening of the vein is small, be quick and apply a sponge soaked in warm water and salt to the place, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has been drawn from the vein. If a black or green mark remains on the spot after a few days, it does no harm; and if you wish, apply something made of aloes or myrrh mixed with juice from calamint, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscess and appearances occur in the bleeding of the basilica; therefore place your hand on it. If you find the place soft upon pressing with your hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said, for perhaps arterial blood is flowing; but make a dry poultice to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, allow it to flow until it is red; and if you see it thick, allow it to flow until it is thinned; and if it is too hot, allow it to cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for someone who is strong and robust, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made, and the incision be wide; and for the weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled little and often, and it should be done by cutting across, and not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood flow and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from the long or wide vein.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to someone whose body weakens during the bleeding, one should give bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, draw blood three or four times.  And if he is of a cold disposition, give him bread soaked in a spiced syrup, or a honey syrup with spices, like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a fragrant syrup, before the bleeding.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the bleeding, after the loss of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to vent his arm and bleed again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the amount of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to vent their arm after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, should bleed again seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another part, should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body, which is already heated and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw a large quantity and widen the opening until it bleeds freely; then you must consider all the conditions of the bleeding, and place your hand on his pulse while he is bleeding, so that death does not come in place of fainting, and this happens many times when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not appropriate when you wish to untie the arm and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press forcefully; nor if it is bent, that he stretch the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but let him bleed the second time; or you prick it with the tip of the flame, so that the blood which is congealed in the vein opening flows forth, and put a little salt in water and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrain it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, bleed him in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled instead of the vein at the top because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in warm water until the vein is red; then it is bound moderately so that the vein appears clearly, then bleed it straight through, not wide or long; and let the opening be wide, and let it bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back into warm water, for it is put more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other vein, as there is neither artery nor nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein at the base of the right hand is good for all liver ailments, and this is the method: restrain the hand, and put it in warm water, until the vein is swollen, so that it can be seen; and if you bleed it through, and if you cut it all the way through, it won't cause any harm; and don't go too deep, for the nerves are under all the exposed flesh, and then put the hand back in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as you need, put oil and a bandage over the vein to close it quickly, and do the same with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the vein in the left hand is good for mice disease, and do just as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bleeding from the vein in the sophene (likely a specific vein location) is good for all ailments below the body, such as aches, retention of flowers, kidney disease, and old thigh and leg ailments, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the method of this bleeding is that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs the vein until it swells, and bind above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and much blood goes from above the foot; bleed it then at the wider vein, or at the ankle, whichever is best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed on the foot, watch out for the nerves underneath, and bleed it through as if cutting; and let the fire be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bleeding fails the first time, start again a little higher up, for the place is salty; but do not fear the nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the vein on the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the heel of the thigh, and its bleeding is good for hip pain, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient enters the bath, and tightens above the ankle with four fingers twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, bleed it in every way you can, and across; and it is better to cut it, for the place is safe, and it is very responsive to the hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, bleed any vein that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make as much blood run as you want, then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and tighten it; it is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	Bloodlettings with cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made of horns, or of bronze, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without striking is done in two ways: either with complete fire, or without fire; and cupping done by striking and extracting blood is done in fourteen places on the body, one of which is on top of the head; and another in the middle of the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and the cupping under the chin; and the cupping on the two shoulders; and the cupping above the buttocks; and the cupping in the middle of the two arms; and the cupping on the two legs; and the cupping on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a person, as is done with vein bleeding; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease arising from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if cupping is necessary for illnesses, or by custom, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at all times; for there are those who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have their tongue swollen, and spit blood; and there are those who dream and see blood and wounds and death and similar things at night.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	Bleeding from the temples helps the heaviness of the head...that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this cupping is in place of bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is not appropriate for those of cold complexion to use it, or those who have a cold, for it does them much harm; and therefore, old people, or those with cold illnesses in their head, should not use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed from it become forgetful, and therefore the cupping should be placed a little lower, for the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping in the neck is a substitute for bleeding from the head and the basilica vein, and therefore it is good for tightness of the breast, and for the constriction of the windpipe, and for coughs, and for fullness; and it should only be applied gently, for if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness in the stomach and in the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia and migraine, and for constriction, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and is a substitute for bleeding from the basilica vein; and you must instruct the practitioner to apply pressure with their hand when applying it, so they do not cut the artery and cause a hemorrhage of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth ailments, and for gum corruption, and similar illnesses in the mouth; and it is a substitute for bleedings from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping on the shoulders is good for ailments caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping on the elbows is as effective as cupping on the three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the practitioner not to press too deep, for the area is devoid of flesh, and is near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	A cupping placed on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for illnesses in the area below, and the cupping must be large and made of bronze, because it needs to draw well; and if it were thin, it might break; and it can cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping on the legs draws blood openly, because it draws blood from the entire body, and is good for long-standing pains in the kidneys, bladder, and uterus, and it removes the inflammation; and they are a substitute for the two soles and two ankles, and however, they weaken the body after prolonged use, and cause pallor in several conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cupping is to first place it empty, and suck gently, and apply it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease this action until you see the area reddened and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then, release, and replace the cupping, and be careful of the body's condition, for some have thick flesh, and clear pores: if this is the case, strike only once, and make broad wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to make the thick blood flow more easily.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out little blood gradually, one strike is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we should repeat the process often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the goal is to pierce the skin quickly, and for those with thick, hard skin and narrow pores, you should apply a stimulating and dissolving oil to the cupping sites: if it is summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if it is winter, use cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amarantin oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person being treated has soft skin and large pores, no oil should be applied, but the area should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or morel water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with a lot of moisture should use willow bark, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with large excesses should use old wine, or oak water, or an anise or chamomile decoction, or other similar things; and one should not bleed with a cupping vessel before or during a bath, but after the bath, one or two hours later; and they should not sleep after being cupped, and they should wash themselves when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch if the person being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; they should take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things; and eat small fish, and hare meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and middling fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat small fish, small birds, and pigeons; and the day they are to be cupped, they should drink more than eat; and sometimes one should give some men a trifle or nutmeg before or after the cupping, to strengthen the main limbs; and let the blood be diluted, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping vessels that are placed without striking are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly, the sides, kidneys, and hip, because those members cannot tolerate being struck on them, and this is done only to draw blood from one limb to another, as we place them on the breasts when the nipple bleeds; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place cupping vessels on the belly and the sides to make the limb thinner; and it relieves pain, when there is obstruction or stone, it removes the obstruction by its attractive virtue, or dislodges the stone from its place; and so it does when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these cupping vessels are administered empty to only suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cupping vessel with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have one small hole near the middle, as for pushing a needle, and it should be of tin, smooth on the front so that it does not injure the patient when placed on the limb; and it should have a cross-shaped rod of tin or iron in the middle, to place a lit candle on, and there should be large and small ones according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the cupping vessels of children are different from those of the old, and from the thin ones to the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping vessel on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or liniment, and place it in the middle of the cupping vessel through the rod that is in the cupping vessel, so that the light is at the bottom of the cupping vessel so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be on the hole that we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor goes out, and one removes the cupping vessel; and one takes the liniment as before, and repeats it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping vessel, then, which is administered in a pleurisy illness, with water only, there is no rod or hole, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only; and this is the form:
