Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only administered on limbs where cupping vessels cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places devoid of flesh, such as toes or noses, and others similar; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in clear fresh water without wounds, you take them; and you place them in fresh water for a night, until they are plump, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let them be drained from a vein or cupping vessel, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the leeches on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where one can put a cupping vessel, then put one, for this is very useful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the place of the wound, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the wound bleeds too much after the leeches have passed, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the blood is stopped; and if the blood is excessive, then put crushed vitriol, or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped; or you put half of peeled beans on the place, and let them until they burn the place, and it will stop immediately; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not want to bite, then rub the place with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle until blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will bite; and when you see that they fall off, then sprinkle a little powdered alum and salt, or ashes, and they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish men are excluded from this chapter, because they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read any of the writings; and for this reason, knowledge is estranged in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have dealt with the knowledge, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have just described in this chapter what is contained, and have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are administered, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, therefore, that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of the discourse and the chapters where the wise man applies his understanding, and remains upon the truth, so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twisting, or crushing occurs to someone, you must quickly bleed the patient from one side and the other, if nothing else prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and avoid cold meats, that is to say, cold joints, and the flesh of birds and young deer, and drink no wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, lest you fear a hot abscess or the spreading of matter to the limb; so that the patient returns to the former way of life that he has been accustomed to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to be restored, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause great nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and thighs, and feet, and cow's belly, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the fracture heals more quickly and easily.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well repaired or mended according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor those of the very young, such as bones of young children; but there is a remedy, to bind the broken bone with thick bandages that hold and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and it is not entirely finished, and therefore it needs to be nourished with nourishing foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the arm, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go in a spiral, and others in a sharp manner, like the blade of a writing pen.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind there is its own device and its own specific instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings to its place; and a fracture of the bone is recognized by its twisted place, and is clearly revealed by a gap, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound on touching, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Therefore, you should not move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that will come later, and then gently hold it steady.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that a spiral fracture, where the two parts are separated, must be carefully aligned, lest a hot abscess arise; and if a hot abscess arises, leave it for a while, until the abscess subsides; then align it as easily and wisely as possible, and know that the restoration of this type is easier than that of one with broken pieces; then hold it steady as is appropriate afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, extend it from two sides, whether it is a hand or a foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you bring back all the additions to their places as best as you can, and be careful that no injury or pain comes to the patient from your work; and properly join the two ends of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not properly aligned: align it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those do who cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is properly aligned, carefully instruct the patient not to move it, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not properly aligned, and it must be placed in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed straight, so that no twisting occurs when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in smallness and largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar ones: soft and fine linen cloths must be wrapped around them; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: they must be wrapped with a wide and hard bandage, because wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and compress it equally on all sides, so that there is no unevenness; then tie around light padding, 3 or 4 turns depending on the limb, and lightly compress the entire bandage with your hand, then move above the fracture and compress it less, so that you pull the fracture apart slightly; and soften the bandage little by little, until you have taken a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it again around the broken area; then return to the area below the fracture and compress it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put linen pads or cloths between the bandages, until everything is even, then tie everything with a strip, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a warming, abscess-soothing thing, and that which removes the swelling, and leave it thus for a few days; then place your splints on top, and let them be half the width of a wisely cut large cane, or of the wood from which cleaves are made, or of palm fronds, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the splint placed over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and also as long as necessary for the limb, whether small or large; then compress the splints as you did in the first chapter, then tie a bandage over them, as in the first chapter over the fracture; tighter on top, gradually less so; and the bandage should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the bandage is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bandages with twisted linen ropes, and that is a great mistake, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than a finger's width of space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the ends of the splints after tightening them in healthy places, put linen pads or soft wool between them so that he is not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment afterward.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to splint all fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to apply splints immediately, but only after five or seven days, or more, depending on the risk of a hot abscess arising; and here is the method of ancient poultices for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: you must take flour that has been stored in the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it.  This is the common method of poultice for restoring fractures in various conditions, especially for women and young children, because it is neither overly hot nor overly cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of poultice for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take three parts of barley, ladani, enule, asafetida, gum arabic, and mugat, each; five parts of myrrh and aloes; nine parts of alechil. Make them into powder, and mix them with plenty of egg; if the patient's constitution is warm, use this poultice, for it is a good preparation and quickly restores broken bones and is effective for many.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another poultice useful for twists: take mugat and vismalve, each ten parts; myrrh and aloes, each nine parts; acacia six parts; Armenian bole ten parts. Grind well and mix with water or plenty of egg, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another poultice for joints and bones separated from their places, which eases the resulting pain, and is used for fractures and splinters: take new wool, soak it in oil and boiled oil, and place it over the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These poultices do not restore, but they are good for easing a hot abscess, and properly relieve pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another poultice which restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of the earth poppy, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another poultice for the restoration of broken bone and for reducing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, chickpea flour, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another poultice stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mallow, flaxseed, baluster, melilot, and sanicle, and violet and chamomile flowers, of all one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb to restore strength anything other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should put on the broken limb, for restoration, somewhat dry and warm things, like myrrh, aloes, frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of poultice that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair, or bird feathers, and mallow, and flax, equally, and grind them, and make a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then after a while, take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not remove it for several days. And if pain, itching, lack of rest, or swelling comes to the place, hurry and remove the poultice immediately; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and apply it to the area until the itching stops and the pain is relieved; then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool, soaked in rosewater or oil, and bandage it for a night, until you are sure the heat is gone. And if the inflammation of the limb subsides, and the pain is gone, then start a delicate bandage again, with a little poultice, and don't bind it as tightly as before; and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the heat, redness, pain, and swelling are completely gone, and you need a poultice and bandage, you should start again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, do not remove the bandage for three, four, five, or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the break is healed and the flesh approaches; then bind it more tightly than before, and increase its nourishment, as I said before; and if you see the area drying out more than necessary, know that no nourishment will come; therefore, moisten it with warm water, every time you remove the bandage, and every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; through this work, nourishment returns to the limb, and immediately cures the misalignment done by those fools who misalign the limb—that is bad, and it is a risky procedure, and I see no other remedy than patience and straightforward work.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many types of fractures exist, with diverse forms and distinct causes; for there are fractures caused by a sword blow, and the blow removes the entire bone down to the surface beneath it, as a wedge or a log does; and for this reason this type of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone, passing through it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow with a blunt object, or a crack or a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or is upon the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there is a wound that is pierced in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and it causes a piece of bone to sink down, and the place splits open like a blacksmith when they strike the kettles; then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as the head of a child; and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are separated like splinters; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of fractures by the pulling on them, and the investigation by prodding, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary fracture is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs on it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be mindful of the patient's accidents, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, loss of consciousness, stretching, fainting, acute fever, and the eyes becoming swollen and red, and other similar symptoms in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the injured person comes to you first, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the earliest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the tissue beneath the bone be corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone extends to the tissue that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part thus: and it is that you take the head of the injured patient, and uncover the bone in every way you can, and over the surface of the wound more gently than you can, and if any blood flows when uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, then assist it with what is necessary, and you must fill the area with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed and you are sure of any blood flow; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two types of work: one type is that you cut in a narrow incision beforehand, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then place another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are of tempered iron; and work gently so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it around, before you administer incisions with drills, not so deep that they pierce beyond the bone of the head, and there should be a margin or a circle above the point, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one comes to its place from the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all surfaces; and this is the form of the three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place a drill on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then reposition the drill slightly afterward, and do this all around, then cut with the chisels the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw the bone with your hand, or with any of the instruments you have such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful that you do not touch the brain or the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and drawn the bone, it is necessary that you remove the remnants of the bone with any other instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be finer and more subtle than the other chisel; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with the poultices and ointments that we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen says, which is safer; and he recommends it very strongly, and that is his statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture is evident, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular chisel, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only; the part is sharp on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet on top, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and pay close attention to the tissue underneath; if it is attached to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce the tissue, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to remove those rough edges and the scales with a fine rasp, of which you should have various sizes, to apply the most suitable one for each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	So use larger rasps first, and then smaller ones afterwards, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you apply a remedy according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily mastered by those who have dedicated themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the surface is exposed, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so that you do not irritate the surface, and then apply another bandage, and do not tighten it so much that it only holds the wound; and leave it like this for one or two days, until the inflamed abscess has subsided, then remove it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and frankincense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and put it on the wound, and apply these medicines frequently without causing any irritation; and make sure that the wound is kept clean, that you do not leave any ointment, or allow pus to accumulate, because when pus collects on the tissue of the brain, it will spread and fester, and cause great harm to the patient; for when a biting substance is applied to the surface, it will burn on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Be careful, then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is certainly dangerous.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the darkening is not severe except due to the medicine applied, and it has such a power, it is necessary that you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and glue it to a cloth, and put it on the surface; then treat it with the necessary methods until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both upper nasal bones are broken, or one alone, for there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger or a probe into the nasal opening, and place the broken piece of bone against your index finger, and hold it from the outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and make sure the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, you must place it aligned with the head of a small, somewhat thick splint.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, do the same again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if possible; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscesses have subsided, then place strips of linen cloth on the head of the nose, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and the strips should be so large that they fill the nasal openings.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers said that the strips should be soaked in butter and changed every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they must be soaked in a concoction of egg white and powdered millstone; then leave the strip in place until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose in place of strips, and a soft cloth is wrapped around it, and this holds the fracture, and the patient breathes through it; or do what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if a boil develops in the nose while you are working on it, put a cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a bit of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a boil does not develop there, apply a plaster on the outside, made from flour of sesamum and powdered incense, mixed with egg white. Then place light wads on it and do not bind the nose.  And if the nose fracture is small and broken into small pieces, remove it with suitable instruments, then close the fissure and treat with things suitable for closing flesh wounds and making them whole, such as suitable plasters and ointments.  And if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with strips and place lead strips there until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured from below, and there is no surface wound, and the fracture is only on the outside, and not broken in two, but only with indentations inside, it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you place your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, place your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inwards, and hold it steady with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two, you must apply extension from both sides until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or fracture, tie them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then apply a plaster to the broken jaw, and place a double bandage on top; and place a large, well-made splint, or a piece of even leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it securely as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back in order what has changed; and apply a poultice of mill dust with plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after you have removed the plaster; and place light wool over the poultice, and if the plaster remains, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; often he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess arises, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of the bone has been removed; if so, carefully remove it using appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply suitable poultices to it, to encourage the growth of flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken forceps; and the other extends the neck toward the part; then place the fracture evenly with your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round cushion of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder, and make it thick as needed; and extend and lift the shoulder, and hold the cushion with your hand, so that you place the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of the way, because it is deep inside, it is necessary that the patient lie often on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder, and let the assistants push the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then straighten the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, you must split it open; and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any impediment, cut it with one of the surgical knives you have; but put this instrument under the shoulder to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, but is not sharp, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the task; and have two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound you made when you pulled out the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, stitch the wound, and if the opening is small, or you suspect a hot abscess, fill the wound with bandages and splints, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, soak a bandage in rose oil, vinegar, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and cuts, is that you put on the bone the plaster of mill dust and egg white, and place light cloths on top, and place a bolster under the arm, if you need it; then take a very wide bandage, one palm wide, then place a doubled bandage over the cloths, and the plaster; then take a thin strip three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the strip over the fracture, and wrap the bandage over the collarbone, and under the healthy armpit and under the diseased armpit; and apply it from both sides, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture in place, and you see clearly that the strip does not move from the broken bone, then monitor it each day, and when the splint loosens, tighten it; and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the armpit when they sleep to raise the shoulder; this will lessen the fracture of the shoulder by lifting the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until bad accidents occur, for up to twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see it necessary, and tighten and leave it like that until it is restored; and it is restored in a maximum of twenty-eight days, and in less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Often, the shoulder breaks either in a wide area or in the middle, and it is not obvious except by touch; so prepare it according to the shape of the fracture, and reposition it according to its natural shape, in all the ways you can; then place on the area mill dust mixed with egg white, and light cloths, and place a doubled bandage over it; then place a wide and thin strip, a little wider than the shoulder, and if under the strip there is any swelling in any part of the shoulder, fill that swelling with linen cloths so that the strip is even; and then tie it with a wide firm bandage, so that the strip does not move from its place, and examine the bandage every day; and every time it loosens, tighten it, and adjust the strip if it is off its place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is complete, untie it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that moves out of place easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and is not under the skin, then cut it open, and remove it, and do what we have said in the fracture of the shoulder to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the rib
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The ribs are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but they often break on the outside.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends inward, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and vomiting, and perhaps vomiting blood, and swelling appears on the broken bone, and one can feel it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that the patient often lies on their back, and a cushion is placed between their shoulders, then the shoulders are pressed, and the ribs on both sides are joined together with your hands, and carefully placed evenly in all the ways you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the thin layer of salt, or some other light material, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and wrap the bandage around the back, and tighten it properly, and check the bandage every hour, and if it softens, tighten it; and if it needs to be untied, due to corrosion or itching that appears in the area, or pain or an abscess, then hurry and untie it, remove the plaster, and take care of what has come from it with suitable treatments; then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures mostly occur in thick areas behind the back, and near the inside, and they only bend because they are brittle; and one can easily feel this during examination on the outside.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is to put the fracture back in place, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a plaster and bind it tightly with a bandage, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is leaning inward, the patient feels very great pain and a stabbing sensation, as if from splinters, because the bone pierces the tissue; and breathes in sharp gasps, and coughs and vomits a great deal of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have devised great remedies for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one should administer foods that inflate the stomach, to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest a hot abscess form, if it has not already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has formed, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say that cupping should be applied to the area, to draw out the matter forcefully, and that seems reasonable; however, there is concern that the cupping may draw the superfluities to the area due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly wrap the wound, then treat it with the pleurisy treatment, diet, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels intense pain that he cannot endure due to the bone piercing the flesh, and the patient is concerned, it is necessary to cut open the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the surface; and then one must cut through the bone, and draw gently, and then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses arise, apply cloths soaked in rose oil to the area; and treat the area as is appropriate for an abscess, and keep the patient often resting on the affected side until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and often it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will heal or not, observe if you see their hands softened and swollen and lifeless, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if they move them and feel them well when squeezed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, observe if the feet are softened, and if the symptoms are present that are in the hands, and on the back there is wind and discharge without will; and when one lies on their stomach, there is discharge without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when they are lying on their back and they want to sit up, they cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not labor in their cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not come to them, the matter is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you observe if there is a hot abscess, then put rose oil or egg yolk oil on the spine until it is soothed; then put one of the comforting and drying plasters on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone separates, it is necessary to cut on the inside; and remove the bone, then bring the two edges of the wound together, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with a grease that causes the flesh to grow, until it is healed; and if the bone's head is broken, which is called the "head of the knee," then put the palm of your left hand on it, and align it with your other hand to the best of your ability, then put the plaster and the splint on top, if you need them; then tie it tightly, and if there is any separated bone, then cut it open, and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, there is not much reduction in the head; and it splits lengthwise, and moves inward, and causes pain and a prick in the affected area, and the injured area swells.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, until you are above the fracture; and find out what is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then put that fracture in alignment, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it moves inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that the restoration of this fracture will be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it in alignment, then place a plaster on it, then put a wooden or leather splint on it, and bind the fracture, so that it does not move; and fill the space under the ribs, until the affected area is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess comes there, do not touch it until the hot abscess has calmed down, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as necessary, if there is no bad accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the ribs and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two methods: of which one is that you take a piece of wood of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two cords to the two ends, and hang them upwards, and have the patient sit on a seat; then place the patient's broken arm on the wood, until it reaches the armpit, and have a bend of wood in the middle, then hang it on some heavy object or the assistant extends it downwards; then the assistant places the fracture equal to his hands together, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on a stretcher, and binds the hand to their neck, then commands two assistants that one hold what is above the fracture with their hands, and the other hold below with a single cord, and each extends to their respective side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, then tighten a cord below the fracture, and above the fracture, and each of the assistants extend to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you place one cord under the armpit, and another towards the ribs, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the ribs, it is necessary to put a cord lightly, without effort, until the fracture is equal above the place, and above the ribs; then place the fracture evenly, as is necessary, and tighten it, if no abscesses are present.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if suppurating abscesses appear, then do not tighten it for seven days, and place soaked wool in oil and rose oil, until the suppurating abscess is soothed; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening it is that you place a plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and place the bandage, and tighten on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in the position of straightness, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone has not shifted.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will shift, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one finger's width of space, and each splint should be so large that it extends three fingers' width on each side beyond the fracture; then tighten over the splints, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter concerning the fracture, more strongly and less as time goes on.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints and the tightening, as we have said, at the time you restore the fractured limb, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave it untied until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the bandage every three days, to ensure that itching, swelling, or inflammation do not appear in the area, or that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is correctly aligned, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, and have their hands on their stomach; and place one cushion full of wool beneath the shoulder, and check every hour of the day or night that the shape of the fractured limb does not move, or that the bandages are not softened; if it is correctly aligned by the virtue of medicine, and give the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a manner that the food is subtle at first; and when it begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be healed in 40 days altogether; and then it should be loosened and administered baths and medicinal ointments to properly align the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is severe and swollen, it remains unloosened for 50 days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
