And when the dislocation is outward, let the patient lie down, as we said for those with a swelling, and bind a rope around the affected leg and also around the foot; then place two sticks, one at the top and one at the bottom, then place a stick between the patient's thighs in the middle; and have damp cloths spread around to prevent injury, then let each assistant pull towards themselves, and let the assistant put an equal amount of force on their side to correct the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, and press it as we described for the swelling, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, the affected leg must be extended quickly, and according to what I have said; and the assistant should put their effort on the affected limb, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is outward, the patient should not be extended downwards, nor lifted from the ground, but rather positioned as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we described for lying on both hips; and let them lie on their face, and the bandage be extended as we said before, and one should press on the joint against the table; and it will be correct when the patient extends their legs, and they are even; then join the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind it with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let them rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and apply the plaster; and if you see that they are even, bind it as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind it, and let the limb heal gradually, until the limb is strong.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward, outward, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not fit against their thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration for all of them is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their face, and place their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and another assistant should extend their foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they can easily bend their leg at the thigh; and apply a plaster, and make the leg bend at the thigh, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then unbind it; and the patient should not walk until the limb is strong.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not correctly aligned, administer strong extension, as we described in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes dislocated, and sometimes completely dislocated, inwards and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and protruding towards the part where it is dislocated: the repositioning is gentle, and one should gently extend it in their hands when it is only dislodged.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and have two assistants hold firmly on the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, then extend it upwards, and push the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, restart the procedure, because it will return; and if it cannot return like this, have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a firm stake in the ground between their thighs, and tie straps around it so it does not injure the patient; then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot in their hands or with a rope tied to the top of the foot; then each assistant extends equally, and the stake remains between the patient's thighs to hold the patient while they are being stretched; then position the dislocated joint in their hands, and another assistant holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is in place, apply a plaster and bandages, and bind the foot firmly to the leg, and guard the nerves above the ankle behind, so the bandages are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, tighten them; then untie them on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before that time, there is no certainty that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a painful abscess arises, you must treat it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, they should be gently extended without any difficulty, and it is an easy matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, you should make the patient sit on a flat surface, or a table, perfectly upright, and place your foot on the exposed joint, then press firmly on your foot until it returns; and when it is aligned and nothing is visible, place a table with two supports under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and allow it to rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies:  do not be presumptuous in the treatment unless you are skillful in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, but not rash; and at first, use soothing hot poultices on the abscess, and leave the patient in the hands of God if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then promptly restore the limb to its place before the abscess becomes hot; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing hot poultices, and treat the wound as necessary with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are separated, remove them and do as we have said in simpler illnesses; and be careful of entering into a state of fear, as I have stated, for it is worthy of reproach according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arms and body.
Amen	Amen
